	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">John F. Kennedy assassination conspiracy theories</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_F._Kennedy_motorcade,_Dallas_crop.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png/220px-John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png/330px-John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png/440px-John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png 2x" data-file-width="3641" data-file-height="2444" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_F._Kennedy_motorcade,_Dallas_crop.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">United States President</a> <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Kennedy_Onassis" title="Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis">Mrs. Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Connally" title="Nellie Connally">Mrs. Connally</a> and <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Texas Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Connally" title="John Connally">John Connally</a>, minutes before the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">assassination</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">assassination of John F. Kennedy</a> on November 22, 1963 and the subsequent murder of the prime suspect <a href="/wiki/Lee_Harvey_Oswald" title="Lee Harvey Oswald">Lee Harvey Oswald</a> by night club owner <a href="/wiki/Jack_Ruby" title="Jack Ruby">Jack Ruby</a> two days later has spurred numerous <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theories" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy theories">conspiracy theories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Summers_1998_p._346_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Summers_1998_p._346-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> These include accusations of involvement of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Italian-American_Mafia" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian-American Mafia">Mafia</a>, sitting <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President</a> <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cuba" title="Prime Minister of Cuba">Cuban Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>, the <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a>, or some combination thereof. The seriously flawed original FBI investigation and Warren Commission report as well as a "benign CIA cover-up" has led to the claim that US federal government deliberately covered up crucial information in the aftermath of the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-politico-benign-coverup_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politico-benign-coverup-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Former Los Angeles District Attorney <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Bugliosi" title="Vincent Bugliosi">Vincent Bugliosi</a> estimated that a total of 42 groups, 82 assassins, and 214 people had been accused at one time or another in various conspiracy scenarios.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1964, the <a href="/wiki/Warren_Commission" title="Warren Commission">Warren Commission</a> concluded that Oswald was the only person responsible for assassinating Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> In 1979, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations" title="United States House Select Committee on Assassinations">United States House Select Committee on Assassinations</a> (HSCA) concluded that Kennedy was assassinated probably as a result of a conspiracy.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-SI_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-SI-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HSCA_Report_0048a_pp._65-75_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSCA_Report_0048a_pp._65-75-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The HSCA concluded that a second gunman besides Oswald probably also fired at Kennedy, based on acoustic evidence that was later discredited.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007377_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007377-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Campbell2008_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell2008-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ATY_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATY-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48_years_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48_years-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Knight2007_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight2007-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Olmsted2011_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olmsted2011-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1998, the Assassinations Records Review Board unearthed inconsistencies in the prior investigations, and the Board's chief analyst for military records contended that the brain photographs in the Kennedy records were probably not of Kennedy's brain.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">Assassination of John F. Kennedy</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy_in_popular_culture" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy in popular culture">Assassination of John F. Kennedy in popular culture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wanted_for_treason.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Wanted_for_treason.jpg/220px-Wanted_for_treason.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="290" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Wanted_for_treason.jpg/330px-Wanted_for_treason.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Wanted_for_treason.jpg/440px-Wanted_for_treason.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="593" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wanted_for_treason.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Handbill circulated on November 21, 1963, one day before the assassination.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> was assassinated by gunshot while traveling in a motorcade in an open-top <a href="/wiki/SS-100-X" title="SS-100-X">limousine</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas, Texas</a> at 12:30&#160;pm CST on Friday, November 22, 1963; Texas Governor <a href="/wiki/John_Connally" title="John Connally">John Connally</a> was wounded, but he survived. Within two hours, <a href="/wiki/Lee_Harvey_Oswald" title="Lee Harvey Oswald">Lee Harvey Oswald</a> was arrested for killing Dallas policeman <a href="/wiki/J._D._Tippit" title="J. D. Tippit">J. D. Tippit</a> and arraigned that evening. Shortly after 1:30&#160;am on Saturday, November 23, Oswald was arraigned for murdering President Kennedy as well.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> On Sunday, November 24, at 11:21&#160;a.m, Mafia associated nightclub owner <a href="/wiki/Jack_Ruby" title="Jack Ruby">Jack Ruby</a> fatally shot Oswald as he was being transferred from the city jail to the county jail.
</p><p>Immediately after the shooting, many people suspected that the assassination was part of a larger plot,<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting" title="Broadcasting">broadcasters</a> speculated that Dallas <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">right-wingers</a> were involved.<sup id="cite_ref-The_New_York_Times;_January_5,_1992_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_New_York_Times;_January_5,_1992-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>  Ruby's shooting of Oswald compounded initial suspicions.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Among conspiracy theorists, author <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lane_(author)" title="Mark Lane (author)">Mark Lane</a> has been described as writing "the first literary shot" with his article, "Defense Brief for Oswald", in the <i><a href="/wiki/National_Guardian" title="National Guardian">National Guardian</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s December 19, 1963 issue.<sup id="cite_ref-Bugliosi_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bugliosi-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Thomas Buchanan's book <i>Who Killed Kennedy?</i>, published in May 1964, has been credited as the first book to allege a conspiracy.<sup id="cite_ref-Donovan_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Donovan-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1964, the <a href="/wiki/Warren_Commission" title="Warren Commission">Warren Commission</a> concluded that Oswald had acted alone and that no credible evidence supported the contention that he was involved in a conspiracy to assassinate the president.<sup id="cite_ref-WCR-C6_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCR-C6-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The Commission also indicated that then-Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Dean_Rusk" title="Dean Rusk">Dean Rusk</a>, then-Defense Secretary <a href="/wiki/Robert_S._McNamara" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert S. McNamara">Robert S. McNamara</a>, then-Treasury Secretary <a href="/wiki/C._Douglas_Dillon" title="C. Douglas Dillon">C. Douglas Dillon</a>, then-Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a>, then-FBI director <a href="/wiki/J._Edgar_Hoover" title="J. Edgar Hoover">J. Edgar Hoover</a>, then-CIA director <a href="/wiki/John_A._McCone" title="John A. McCone">John A. McCone</a>, and then-Secret Service Chief <a href="/wiki/James_J._Rowley" class="mw-redirect" title="James J. Rowley">James J. Rowley</a>, each individually reached the same conclusion on the basis of information available to them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964374_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964374-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Trial_of_Clay_Shaw" title="Trial of Clay Shaw">trial of Clay Shaw</a> in 1969, however, <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> District Attorney <a href="/wiki/Jim_Garrison" title="Jim Garrison">Jim Garrison</a> challenged the <a href="/wiki/Single-bullet_theory" title="Single-bullet theory">single-bullet theory</a> with evidence from the <a href="/wiki/Zapruder_film" title="Zapruder film">Zapruder film</a>, which he claimed indicated that a fourth shot from the <a href="/wiki/Dealey_Plaza" title="Dealey Plaza">grassy knoll</a> had caused the fatal shot to Kennedy's head.
</p><p>In 1979, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations" title="United States House Select Committee on Assassinations">United States House Select Committee on Assassinations</a> (HSCA) agreed with the Warren Commission that Oswald did, in fact, assassinate Kennedy, but concluded that the Commission's report and the original FBI investigation were seriously flawed. The HSCA concluded that at least four shots were fired with a "high probability" that two gunmen fired at the President, and that a conspiracy to do so was probable.<sup id="cite_ref-HSCA_Report_0048a_pp._65-75_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSCA_Report_0048a_pp._65-75-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The HSCA stated that the Warren Commission had "failed to investigate adequately the possibility of a conspiracy to assassinate the President".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_assassination#Ramsey_Clark_Panel" class="mw-redirect" title="John F. Kennedy assassination">Ramsey Clark Panel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_assassination#Rockefeller_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="John F. Kennedy assassination">Rockefeller Commission</a> both supported the Warren Commission's conclusions.
</p><p>Most of the documents under Section 5 of the <a href="/wiki/President_John_F._Kennedy_Assassination_Records_Collection_Act_of_1992" title="President John F. Kennedy Assassination Records Collection Act of 1992">President John F. Kennedy Assassination Records Collection Act of 1992</a> were released on October 26, 2017, while the remaining documents that are still classified will be analyzed for redactions.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> A deadline for the remaining documents to be released has been set for October 26, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_opinion">Public opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Public opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to author <a href="/wiki/John_C._McAdams" title="John C. McAdams">John C. McAdams</a>, "[t]he greatest and grandest of all conspiracy theories is the Kennedy assassination conspiracy theory."<sup id="cite_ref-Krajicek_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krajicek-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Others have often referred to it as "the mother of all conspiracies".<sup id="cite_ref-Broderick_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Broderick-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Perry_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perry-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The number of books written about the assassination of Kennedy has been estimated to be between 1,000<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007xiv_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007xiv-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007974_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007974-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and 2,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Bugliosi" title="Vincent Bugliosi">Vincent Bugliosi</a>, 95% of those books are "pro-conspiracy and anti-Warren Commission".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007xiv_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007xiv-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Author David Krajicek describes Kennedy assassination enthusiasts as people belonging to "<a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theorists" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy theorists">conspiracy theorists</a>" on one side and "<a href="/wiki/Debunkers" class="mw-redirect" title="Debunkers">debunkers</a>" on the other.<sup id="cite_ref-Krajicek_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krajicek-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The great amount of controversy surrounding the event has resulted in bitter disputes between those who support the conclusion of the Warren Commission and those who reject it, or are critical of the official explanation with each side levelling toward the other accusations of "naivete, cynicism, and selective interpretation of the evidence".<sup id="cite_ref-Perry_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perry-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Public opinion polls have consistently shown that most Americans believe there was a conspiracy to kill President Kennedy. However, on the question of a government cover-up, different polls show both a minority and a majority of Americans who believe the government was engaged in one.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> These same polls also show no agreement on who else may have been involved in the shooting. A 2003 <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)#Gallup_Poll" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup Poll</a> reported that 75% of Americans do not believe that Lee Harvey Oswald had acted alone.<sup id="cite_ref-Lydia_Saad_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lydia_Saad-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> That same year, an <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a> poll found that 70% of respondents suspected that the assassination involved more than one person.<sup id="cite_ref-langer20031116_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-langer20031116-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> A 2004 <a href="/wiki/Fox_News_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Fox News Channel">Fox News</a> poll noted that 66% of Americans thought there had been a conspiracy while 74% believed that there was a cover-up.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, 76% of people polled for <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a> said they believed the President had been killed as the result of a conspiracy.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> A 2013 Gallup Poll found that 61% of Americans, the lowest figure in nearly 50 years, believed other people besides Oswald were involved.<sup id="cite_ref-Gallup,_Inc_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gallup,_Inc-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Circumstantial_evidence_of_a_cover-up">Circumstantial evidence of a cover-up</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Circumstantial evidence of a cover-up">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_2">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After Oswald was shot dead by Ruby, <a href="/wiki/J._Edgar_Hoover" title="J. Edgar Hoover">FBI Director Hoover</a> wrote a memo detailing that the Dallas Police would not have had enough evidence against Oswald without the FBI's information. He then wrote: "The thing I am concerned about, and so is [Deputy Attorney General] <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Katzenbach" title="Nicholas Katzenbach">Mr. Katzenbach</a>, is having something issued so we can convince the public that Oswald is the real assassin."<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Top government and intelligence officials were also finding that, according to CIA intercepts, someone had impersonated Oswald in phone calls made to the Soviet embassy.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Over the next 40 years this became one of the CIA’s most closely guarded secrets on the Oswald case.<sup id="cite_ref-PBS_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBS-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> A CIA career agency officer, Anne Goodpasture, admitted in sworn testimony that she had disseminated the tapes of these phone calls herself. She had earlier denied to congressional investigators in 1970 that she had any knowledge of recordings of Oswald’s phone calls.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With the information that someone had been impersonating Oswald, <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">President Johnson</a> expressed concern that the public might come to believe that Khrushchev and/or Castro was implicated in the assassination — a situation that Johnson said might lead to "... a war that [could] kill 40 million Americans in an hour". Johnson relayed his concern to both <a href="/wiki/Earl_Warren" title="Earl Warren">Chief Justice Earl Warren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Russell_Jr." title="Richard Russell Jr.">Senator Richard Russell</a>, telling them that they could "serve America" by joining the commission Johnson had established to investigate the assassination, which would later become known unofficially as the <a href="/wiki/Warren_Commission" title="Warren Commission">Warren Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PBS_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBS-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In turn, Katzenbach wrote a memorandum to Lyndon Johnson aide <a href="/wiki/Bill_Moyers" title="Bill Moyers">Bill Moyers</a> that said, among other things, that the results of the FBI's investigation should be made public.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Katzenbach also suggested that a commission be formed, composed of people with "impeccable integrity" to conduct a complete investigation of the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Katzenbach wrote: "Speculation about Oswald’s motivation ought to be cut off, and we should have some basis for rebutting thought that this was a Communist conspiracy or (as the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> press is saying) a right–wing conspiracy to blame it on the Communists." He also wrote: "The public must be satisfied that Oswald was the assassin; that he did not have confederates who are still at large; and that the evidence was such that he would have been convicted at trial".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Four days after Katzenbach's memo, Johnson formed the Warren Commission with Earl Warren as chairman and Senator Richard Russell as a member.<sup id="cite_ref-Savage_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Savage-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Numerous researchers, author <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lane_(author)" title="Mark Lane (author)">Mark Lane</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Henry Hurt,<sup id="cite_ref-Hurt_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hurt-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_L._Kurtz" title="Michael L. Kurtz">Michael L. Kurtz</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Gerald D. McKnight,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Summers" title="Anthony Summers">Anthony Summers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Summers_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Summers-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Harold_Weisberg" title="Harold Weisberg">Harold Weisberg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> have pointed out what they characterize as inconsistencies, oversights, exclusions of evidence, errors, changing stories, or changes made to witness testimony in the official Warren Commission investigation, which they say could suggest a cover-up.
</p><p>Michael Benson wrote that the Warren Commission received only information supplied to it by the FBI, and that its purpose was to <a href="/wiki/Rubber_stamp_(politics)" title="Rubber stamp (politics)">rubber stamp</a> the <a href="/wiki/Lone_gunman_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Lone gunman theory">lone gunman theory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Benson_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benson-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>United States Senator and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Senate_Select_Committee_on_Intelligence" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Senate Select Committee on Intelligence">U.S. Senate Select Committee on Intelligence</a> member <a href="/wiki/Richard_Schweiker" title="Richard Schweiker">Richard Schweiker</a> told author Anthony Summers in 1978 that he "believe[d] that the Warren Commission was set up at the time to feed pabulum to the American public for reasons not yet known, and that one of the biggest cover-ups in the history of our country occurred at that time".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers2013243_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers2013243-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/James_H._Fetzer" title="James H. Fetzer">James H. Fetzer</a> took issue with a 1998 statement from Federal Judge and Assassination Records Review Board (ARRB) Chairman <a href="/wiki/John_R._Tunheim" title="John R. Tunheim">John R. Tunheim</a>, who stated that no "<a href="/wiki/Smoking_gun" title="Smoking gun">smoking guns</a>" indicating a conspiracy or cover-up were discovered during their efforts in the early 1990s to declassify documents related to the assassination. Fetzer identified 16 "smoking guns" that he claims prove the official narrative is impossible, and therefore a conspiracy and cover-up occurred. He also claims that evidence released by the ARRB substantiates these concerns. These include problems with bullet trajectories, the murder weapon, the ammunition used, inconsistencies between the Warren Commission's account and the autopsy findings, inconsistencies between the autopsy findings and what was reported by witnesses at the scene of the murder, eyewitness accounts that conflict with x-rays taken of the President's body, indications that the diagrams and photos of the President's brain in the <a href="/wiki/National_Archives_and_Records_Administration" title="National Archives and Records Administration">National Archives</a> are not the President's, testimony by those who took and processed the autopsy photos that the photos were altered, created, or destroyed, indications that the <a href="/wiki/Zapruder_film" title="Zapruder film">Zapruder film</a> had been tampered with, allegations that the Warren Commission's version of events conflicts with news reports from the scene of the murder, an alleged change to the motorcade route that facilitated the assassination, alleged lax Secret Service and local law enforcement security, and statements made by people who claim that they had knowledge of, or participated in, a conspiracy to kill the President.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1966, <a href="/wiki/Roscoe_Drummond" title="Roscoe Drummond">Roscoe Drummond</a> voiced skepticism about a cover-up in his syndicated column, saying, "If there were a conspiracy to cover up the truth about the assassination, it would have to involve the Chief Justice, the Republican, Democratic, and non-party members of the commission, the FBI, the CIA, the Secret Service, the distinguished doctors of the armed services — and the White House — a conspiracy so multiple and complex that it would have fallen of its own weight."<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Allegations_of_witness_tampering.2C_intimidation.2C_and_foul_play"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_witness_tampering,_intimidation,_and_foul_play">Allegations of witness tampering, intimidation, and foul play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Allegations of witness tampering, intimidation, and foul play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alleged_witness_intimidation">Alleged witness intimidation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Alleged witness intimidation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Richard Buyer wrote that many witnesses whose statements pointed to a conspiracy were either ignored or <a href="/wiki/Witness_intimidation" class="mw-redirect" title="Witness intimidation">intimidated</a> by the Warren Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-Buyer_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buyer-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In <i>JFK: The Last Dissenting Witness</i>, a 1992 biography of <a href="/wiki/Jean_Hill" title="Jean Hill">Jean Hill</a>, Bill Sloan wrote that Warren Commission assistant counsel <a href="/wiki/Arlen_Specter" title="Arlen Specter">Arlen Specter</a> attempted to humiliate, discredit, and intimidate Hill into changing her story. Hill also told Sloan that she was abused by Secret Service agents, harassed by the FBI, and received death threats.<sup id="cite_ref-Sloan_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloan-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A later book by Sloan, entitled <i>JFK: Breaking the Silence</i>, quotes several assassination eyewitnesses as saying that Warren Commission interviewers repeatedly cut short or stifled any comments casting doubt on the conclusion that Oswald had acted alone.
</p><p>In his book <i>Crossfire</i>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Marrs" title="Jim Marrs">Jim Marrs</a> gives accounts of several people who said they were intimidated by either FBI agents or anonymous individuals into altering or suppressing what they knew regarding the assassination. Some of those individuals include Richard Carr, Acquilla Clemmons, Sandy Speaker, and A. J. Millican.<sup id="cite_ref-Marrs_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marrs-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Marrs also wrote that Texas School Book Depository employee Joe Molina was "intimidated by authorities and lost his job soon after the assassination",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs198987_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs198987-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> and that witness Ed Hoffman was warned by an FBI agent that he "might get killed" if he revealed what he observed in <a href="/wiki/Dealey_Plaza" title="Dealey Plaza">Dealey Plaza</a> on the day of the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs198988_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs198988-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Witness_deaths">Witness deaths</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Witness deaths">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Allegations of mysterious or suspicious deaths of witnesses connected with the Kennedy assassination originated with <a href="/wiki/Penn_Jones,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Penn Jones, Jr.">Penn Jones, Jr.</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-IV_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-IV-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi20071012,_1276_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi20071012,_1276-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> and were brought to national attention by the 1973 film <i><a href="/wiki/Executive_Action_(film)" title="Executive Action (film)">Executive Action</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-IV_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-IV-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi20071012_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi20071012-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Jim Marrs later presented a list of 103 people he believed died "convenient deaths" under suspicious circumstances. He noted that the deaths were grouped around investigations conducted by the Warren Commission, New Orleans D.A. <a href="/wiki/Jim_Garrison" title="Jim Garrison">Jim Garrison</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Select_Committee_on_Intelligence" title="United States Senate Select Committee on Intelligence">Senate Intelligence Committee</a>, and the House Select Committee on Assassinations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989555–566_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989555–566-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Marrs pointed out that "these deaths certainly would have been convenient for anyone not wishing the truth of the JFK assassination to become public."<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Belzer" title="Richard Belzer">Richard Belzer</a> published <i>Hit List: An In-Depth Investigation into the Mysterious Deaths of Witnesses to the JFK Assassination</i> that examines the deaths of 50 people linked to the assassination and claims they were murdered as part of a cover-up.<sup id="cite_ref-Elias_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elias-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vincent_Bugliosi" title="Vincent Bugliosi">Vincent Bugliosi</a> devoted two pages of his book Reclaiming History to journalist <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Kilgallen" title="Dorothy Kilgallen">Dorothy Kilgallen</a>. On February 23, 1964, the New York City newspaper where she was employed published her article about a conversation she had had with Jack Ruby when he was at his defense table surrounded by his lawyers during a recess in his murder trial. Whether Kilgallen and Ruby had a second conversation in a private room in the courthouse several days later has been disputed.   If they did, she never wrote about it for publication.  Bugliosi referred to Kilgallen’s 1965 death as "perhaps the most prominent mysterious death" cited by assassination researchers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi20071014_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi20071014-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>According to author Jerome Kroth, Mafia figures <a href="/wiki/Sam_Giancana" title="Sam Giancana">Sam Giancana</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Roselli" title="John Roselli">John Roselli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Prio" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlos Prio">Carlos Prio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Hoffa" title="Jimmy Hoffa">Jimmy Hoffa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Nicoletti" title="Charles Nicoletti">Charles Nicoletti</a>, Leo Moceri, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cain" title="Richard Cain">Richard Cain</a>, Salvatore Granello, and Dave Yaras were likely murdered to prevent them from revealing their knowledge.<sup id="cite_ref-Kroth_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kroth-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> According to author Matthew Smith, others with some tie to the case who have died suspicious deaths include <a href="/wiki/Lee_Bowers" title="Lee Bowers">Lee Bowers</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Garrett_Underhill,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="John Garrett Underhill, Jr.">Gary Underhill</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_C._Sullivan" title="William C. Sullivan">William Sullivan</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Ferrie" title="David Ferrie">David Ferrie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clay_Shaw" title="Clay Shaw">Clay Shaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_de_Mohrenschildt" title="George de Mohrenschildt">George de Mohrenschildt</a>, four showgirls who worked for Jack Ruby, and Ruby himself.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The House Select Committee on Assassinations investigated another alleged "mysterious death" — that of Rose Cheramie.<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-X_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-X-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The Committee reported that Louisiana State Police Lieutenant Francis Fruge traveled to <a href="/wiki/Eunice,_Louisiana" title="Eunice, Louisiana">Eunice, Louisiana</a>, on November 20, 1963 — two days before the assassination — to pick up Cheramie, who had sustained minor injuries when she was hit by a car.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989401_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989401-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979201_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979201-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Fruge drove Cheramie to the hospital and said that on the way there, she "... related to [him] that she was coming from Florida to Dallas with two men who were Italians or resembled Italians." Fruge asked her what she planned to do in Dallas, to which she replied: "... number one, pick up some money, pick up [my] baby, and ... kill Kennedy."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979201_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979201-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Cheramie was admitted and treated at State Hospital in <a href="/wiki/Jackson,_Louisiana" title="Jackson, Louisiana">Jackson, Louisiana</a> for alcohol and heroin addiction.
</p><p>State Hospital physician Dr. Victor Weiss later told a House Select Committee investigator that on November 25 — three days after the assassination — one of his fellow physicians told him that Cheramie had "stated before the assassination that President Kennedy was going to be killed".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979200_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979200-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Dr. Weiss further reported that Cheramie told him after the assassination that she had worked for Jack Ruby and that her knowledge of the assassination originated from "word in the underworld".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979201_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979201-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> After the assassination, Lt. Fruge contacted Dallas Police Captain Will Fritz regarding what he had learned from Cheramie, but Fritz told him he "wasn't interested".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979202_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979202-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Cheramie was found dead by a highway near <a href="/wiki/Big_Sandy,_Texas" title="Big Sandy, Texas">Big Sandy, Texas</a>, on September 4, 1965; she had been run over by a car.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979199_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAppendix_to_Hearings_before_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Volume_X1979199-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another "suspicious death" cited by Jim Marrs was that of Joseph Milteer, director of the <a href="/wiki/Dixie" title="Dixie">Dixie</a> <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">Klan</a> of Georgia. Milteer was secretly tape-recorded thirteen days before the assassination telling Miami police informant William Somersett that the murder of Kennedy was "in the working". Milteer died in 1974 when a heater exploded in his house.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989562_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989562-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The House Select Committee on Assassinations reported in 1979 that Milteer's information on the threat to the President "was furnished [to] the agents making the advance arrangements before the visit of the President" to Miami, but that "the Milteer threat was ignored by Secret Service personnel in planning the trip to Dallas." Robert Bouck, Special Agent-in-Charge of the Secret Service's Protective Research Section, testified that "threat information was transmitted from one region of the country to another if there was specific evidence it was relevant to the receiving region."<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The House Select Committee on Assassinations investigated the allegation "that a statistically improbable number of individuals with some direct or peripheral association with the Kennedy assassination died as a result of that assassination, thereby raising the specter of conspiracy".<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-IV_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-IV-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The committee's chief of research testified: "Our final conclusion on the issue is that the available evidence does not establish anything about the nature of these deaths which would indicate that the deaths were in some manner, either direct or peripheral, caused by the assassination of President Kennedy or by any aspect of the subsequent investigation."<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-IV_71-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-IV-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Author Gerald Posner said that Marrs's list was taken from the group of about 10,000 people connected even in the most tenuous way to the assassination, including people identified in the official investigations, as well as the research of conspiracy theorists. Posner also said that it would be surprising if a hundred people out of ten thousand did not die in "unnatural ways". He noted that over half of the people on Marrs's list did not die mysteriously, but of natural causes, such as Secret Service agent <a href="/wiki/Roy_Kellerman" title="Roy Kellerman">Roy Kellerman</a>, who died of heart failure at age 69 in 1984, long after the Kennedy assassination, but is on Marrs's list as someone whose cause of death is "unknown". Posner also pointed out that many prominent witnesses and conspiracy researchers continue to live long lives.<sup id="cite_ref-Posner2003_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Posner2003-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Allegations_of_evidence_suppression.2C_tampering.2C_and_fabrication"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_evidence_suppression,_tampering,_and_fabrication">Allegations of evidence suppression, tampering, and fabrication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Allegations of evidence suppression, tampering, and fabrication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Many of those who believe in a JFK assassination conspiracy also believe that evidence against Oswald was either planted, forged, or tampered with.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007984_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007984-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suppression_of_evidence">Suppression of evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Suppression of evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ignored_testimony">Ignored testimony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ignored testimony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Some assassination researchers assert that witness statements indicating a conspiracy were ignored by the Warren Commission. <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Thompson" title="Josiah Thompson">Josiah Thompson</a> stated that the Commission ignored the testimony of seven eyewitnesses who said they saw smoke in the vicinity of the grassy knoll at the time of the assassination, as well as an eighth witness who said he smelled gunpowder.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Jim Marrs wrote that the Commission did not seek the testimony of eyewitnesses on the triple underpass whose statements pointed to a shooter on the grassy knoll.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs198987_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs198987-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Confiscated_film_and_photographs">Confiscated film and photographs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Confiscated film and photographs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Other researchers reported that witnesses who captured the assassination via photographs or film had their cameras confiscated by police or other authorities. Author Jim Marrs and documentary producer Nigel Turner both presented the account of <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Arnold" title="Gordon Arnold">Gordon Arnold</a> who said that his film of the motorcade was taken by two policemen shortly after the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs198988_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs198988-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Another witness, identified as Beverly Oliver, came forward in 1970 and said she was the "<a href="/wiki/Babushka_Lady" title="Babushka Lady">Babushka Lady</a>" who is seen, in the <a href="/wiki/Zapruder_film" title="Zapruder film">Zapruder film</a>, filming the motorcade. She also said that after the assassination, she was contacted at work by two men who she thought "... were either FBI or Secret Service agents". According to Oliver, the men told her that they wanted to develop her film and return it to her within ten days, but they never did so.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs198936_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs198936-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Withheld_documents">Withheld documents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Withheld documents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Richard Buyer and others have complained that many documents pertaining to the assassination have been withheld over the years, including documents from investigations made by the Warren Commission, the House Select Committee on Assassinations, and the Church Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-Buyer_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buyer-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> These documents individually included the President's autopsy records. Some documents still are not scheduled for release until 2029. Many documents were released during the mid-to-late 1990s by the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_Records_Review_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="Assassination Records Review Board">Assassination Records Review Board</a> (ARRB) under the <a href="/wiki/President_John_F._Kennedy_Assassination_Records_Collection_Act_of_1992" title="President John F. Kennedy Assassination Records Collection Act of 1992">President John F. Kennedy Assassination Records Collection Act of 1992</a>. However, some of the material released contains <a href="/wiki/Sanitization_(classified_information)" title="Sanitization (classified information)">redacted</a> sections. Tax return information, which identified employers and sources of income, has not yet been released.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The existence of several secret documents related to the assassination, as well as the long period of secrecy, suggests to some the possibility of a cover-up. One historian noted, "There exists widespread suspicion about the government's disposition of the Kennedy assassination records stemming from the beliefs that Federal officials (1) have not made available all Government assassination records (even to the Warren Commission, Church Committee, House Assassination Committee) and (2) have heavily redacted the records released under FOIA in order to cover up sinister conspiracies."<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> According to the ARRB, "All Warren Commission records, except those records that contain tax return information, are (now) available to the public with only minor redactions."<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In response to a <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_Information_Act_(United_States)" title="Freedom of Information Act (United States)">Freedom of Information Act</a> request filed by journalist Jefferson Morley, the CIA stated in 2010 that it had over 1,100 documents in relation to the assassination, about 2,000 pages in total, that have not been released due to national security-related concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tampering_with_evidence">Tampering with evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tampering with evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some researchers have alleged that various items of physical evidence have been tampered with, including the <a href="/wiki/Single_bullet_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Single bullet theory">"single bullet"</a> (also known as the "magic bullet" by some critics of official explanations), various bullet cartridges and fragments, the <a href="/wiki/SS-100-X" title="SS-100-X">presidential limousine</a>'s windshield, the paper bag in which the Warren Commission said Oswald hid the rifle, the so-called "backyard" photos depicting Oswald holding the rifle, the Zapruder film, the photographs and radiographs obtained at Kennedy's autopsy, and the president's dead body itself.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Photographs">Photographs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Photographs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lho-133A.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Lho-133A.jpg/220px-Lho-133A.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Lho-133A.jpg/330px-Lho-133A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Lho-133A.jpg/440px-Lho-133A.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2306" data-file-height="2280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lho-133A.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oswald, carrying a rifle in his backyard</div></div></div>
<p>Among the evidence against Oswald are <a href="/wiki/Lee_Harvey_Oswald#Backyard_photos" title="Lee Harvey Oswald">photographs of him</a> holding a Carcano rifle — the weapon identified by the Warren Commission as the assassination weapon — in his backyard. The House Select Committee on Assassinations concluded that the Oswald photos are genuine<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> and Oswald's wife, <a href="/wiki/Marina_Oswald_Porter" title="Marina Oswald Porter">Marina</a>, said that she took them.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, the journal <i><a href="/wiki/Perception_(journal)" title="Perception (journal)">Perception</a></i> published the findings of <a href="/wiki/Hany_Farid" title="Hany Farid">Hany Farid</a>, a professor in the Department of Computer Science at <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth College</a>, who used <a href="/wiki/3D_modeling_software" class="mw-redirect" title="3D modeling software">3D modeling software</a> to analyze one of the photographs.<sup id="cite_ref-Hany_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hany-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ramer_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramer-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> After demonstrating that a single light source could create seemingly incongruent shadows, Farid concluded that the photograph revealed no evidence of tampering.<sup id="cite_ref-Hany_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hany-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ramer_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramer-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Many researchers, including <a href="/wiki/Robert_Groden" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Groden">Robert Groden</a>, assert that these photos are fake.<sup id="cite_ref-Groden_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Groden-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1979, after the HSCA had disbanded, Groden said that four autopsy photographs showing the back of Kennedy's head were forged to hide a wound fired from a second gunman.<sup id="cite_ref-Daily_Reporter;_July_9,_1979_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Reporter;_July_9,_1979-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> According to Groden, a photograph of a <a href="/wiki/Cadaver" title="Cadaver">cadaver</a>'s head was <a href="/wiki/Matte_(filmmaking)" title="Matte (filmmaking)">inserted over another</a> depicting a large exit wound in the back of the president's head.<sup id="cite_ref-Daily_Reporter;_July_9,_1979_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Reporter;_July_9,_1979-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> HSCA chief counsel <a href="/wiki/G._Robert_Blakey" title="G. Robert Blakey">G. Robert Blakey</a>, in response to the allegations, stated that the "suggestion that the committee would participate in a cover-up is absurd"<sup id="cite_ref-Observer-Reporter;_July_10,_1979_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Observer-Reporter;_July_10,_1979-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and that Groden was "not competent to make a judgment on whether [or not] a photograph has been altered".<sup id="cite_ref-The_Washington_Post;_July_10,_1979_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Washington_Post;_July_10,_1979-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Blakey stated that the photographic analysis panel for the Committee had examined the photographs and that they "considered everything [Groden] had to say and rejected it."<sup id="cite_ref-Observer-Reporter;_July_10,_1979_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Observer-Reporter;_July_10,_1979-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Washington_Post;_July_10,_1979_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Washington_Post;_July_10,_1979-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Zapruder_film">The Zapruder film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: The Zapruder film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The House Select Committee on Assassinations described the Zapruder film as "the best available photographic evidence of the number and timing of the shots that struck the occupants of the presidential limousine".<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-IA_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-IA-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The Assassination Records Review Board said it "is perhaps the single most important assassination record."<sup id="cite_ref-ARRB-6II_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARRB-6II-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> According to Vincent Bugliosi, the film was "originally touted by the vast majority of conspiracy theorists as incontrovertible proof of [a] conspiracy" but is now believed by many conspiracy theorists to be a "sophisticated forgery".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Among those who believe that the Zapruder film has been altered are John Costella,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_H._Fetzer" title="James H. Fetzer">James H. Fetzer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512_110-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Lifton" title="David Lifton">David Lifton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512_110-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> David Mantik,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512_110-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Jack White,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512_110-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Noel Twyman,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> and Harrison Livingstone, who has called it "the biggest hoax of the 20th century".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512_110-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007504–512-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> In 1996, former Kodak product engineer Roland Zavada was requested by the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_Records_Review_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="Assassination Records Review Board">Assassination Records Review Board</a> to undertake a thorough technical study of the Zapruder Film.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Zavada concluded that there was no detectable evidence of manipulation or image alteration on the film's original version.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>David Lifton wrote that the Zapruder film was in the possession of the CIA's <a href="/wiki/National_Photographic_Interpretation_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="National Photographic Interpretation Center">National Photographic Interpretation Center</a> by the night of the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Jack White, researcher and photographic consultant to the <a href="/wiki/House_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations" class="mw-redirect" title="House Select Committee on Assassinations">House Select Committee on Assassinations</a>, claimed that there were anomalies in the Zapruder film, including an "unnatural jerkiness of movement or change of focus ... in certain frame sequences".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Kennedy.27s_body"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kennedy's_body">Kennedy's body</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Kennedy&#039;s body">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In his 1981 book <i>Best Evidence</i>, author <a href="/wiki/David_Lifton" title="David Lifton">David Lifton</a> presented the thesis that President Kennedy's dead body had been altered between the Dallas hospital and the autopsy site at Bethesda for the purposes of creating erroneous conclusions about the number and direction of the shots.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fabrication_of_evidence">Fabrication of evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Fabrication of evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Murder_weapon">Murder weapon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Murder weapon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Warren Commission found that the shots that killed Kennedy and wounded Connally were fired from an <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_assassination_rifle" title="John F. Kennedy assassination rifle">Italian 6.5mm Manlicher Carcano rifle owned by Oswald</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WCR-C1_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCR-C1-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Deputy Sheriff Eugene Boone and Deputy Constable Seymour Weitzman both initially identified the rifle found in the Texas School Book Depository as a 7.65 <a href="/wiki/Mauser" title="Mauser">Mauser</a>. Weitzman signed an affidavit the following day describing the weapon as a "7.65 Mauser bolt action equipped with a 4/18 scope, a thick leather brownish-black sling on it".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Deputy Sheriff Roger Craig claimed that he saw "7.65 Mauser" stamped on the barrel of the weapon.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> When interviewed in 1968 by Barry Ernest, author of <i>The Girl on the Stairs — The Search for a Missing Witness to the JFK Assassination</i>, Craig said: "I felt then and I still feel now that the weapon was a 7.65 German Mauser .... I was there. I saw it when it was first pulled from its hiding place, and I am not alone in describing it as a Mauser."<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dallas District Attorney <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wade" title="Henry Wade">Henry Wade</a> told the press that the weapon found in the Book Depository was a 7.65 Mauser, and the media reported this.<sup id="cite_ref-WCR-C5_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCR-C5-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> But investigators later identified the rifle as a 6.5mm Carcano.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989439–440_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989439–440-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGroden1995118_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGroden1995118-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In <i>Matrix for Assassination</i>, author Richard Gilbride suggested that both weapons were involved in the assassination and that Dallas Police Captain Will Fritz and Lieutenant J. Carl Day both might have been conspirators.<sup id="cite_ref-Gilbride_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilbride-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Addressing "speculation and rumors", the Warren Commission identified Weitzman as "the original source of the speculation that the rifle was a Mauser" and stated that "police laboratory technicians subsequently arrived and correctly identified the [murder] weapon as a 6.5 Italian rifle."<sup id="cite_ref-WCR-A12_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCR-A12-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bullets_and_cartridges">Bullets and cartridges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Bullets and cartridges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Warren Commission determined that three bullets were fired at the presidential motorcade. One of the three bullets missed the vehicle entirely; another bullet hit President Kennedy and passed through his body before striking Governor Connally; and the third bullet was the fatal head shot to the President. Some claim that the bullet that passed through President Kennedy's body and hit Governor Connally — dubbed by critics of the Commission as the "magic bullet" — was missing too little mass to account for the total weight of bullet fragments later found by the doctors who operated on Connally at Parkland Hospital. Those making this claim included the governor's chief surgeon, Dr. Robert Shaw,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> as well as two of Kennedy's autopsy surgeons, Commander James Humes<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> and Lt. Colonel Pierre Finck.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> However, in his book <i>Six Seconds in Dallas</i>, author Josiah Thompson took issue with this claim. Thompson added up the weight of the bullet fragments listed in the doctor reports and concluded that their total weight "could" have been less than the mass missing from the bullet.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With Connally's death in 1993, forensic pathologist Dr. <a href="/wiki/Cyril_Wecht" title="Cyril Wecht">Cyril Wecht</a> and the Assassination Archives and Research Center petitioned <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_General" title="United States Attorney General">Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Janet_Reno" title="Janet Reno">Janet Reno</a> to recover the remaining bullet fragments from Connally's body, contending that the fragments would disprove the Warren Commission's <a href="/wiki/Single-bullet_theory" title="Single-bullet theory">single-bullet</a>, single-gunman conclusion. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">Justice Department</a> replied that it "... would have [had] no legal authority to recover the fragments unless Connally's family gave [it] permission [to do so]." Connally's family refused permission.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_multiple_gunmen">Allegations of multiple gunmen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Allegations of multiple gunmen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dealey_Plaza_2003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Dealey_Plaza_2003.jpg/220px-Dealey_Plaza_2003.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Dealey_Plaza_2003.jpg/330px-Dealey_Plaza_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Dealey_Plaza_2003.jpg/440px-Dealey_Plaza_2003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1818" data-file-height="1228" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dealey_Plaza_2003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dealey_Plaza" title="Dealey Plaza">Dealey Plaza</a> in 2003.</div></div></div>
<p>The Warren Commission concluded that "three shots were fired from the Texas School Book Depository in a time period ranging from approximately 4.8 to in excess of 7 seconds."<sup id="cite_ref-WCR3_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCR3-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Some assassination researchers, including Anthony Summers, dispute the Commission's findings. They point to evidence that brings into question the number of shots fired, the origin of the shots, and Oswald's ability to accurately fire three shots in such a short amount of time from such a rifle.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> These researchers suggest that multiple gunmen were involved.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers201331-_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers201331--136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Number_of_shots">Number of shots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Number of shots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Based on the "consensus among the witnesses at the scene" and "in particular the three spent cartridges", the Warren Commission determined that "the preponderance of the evidence indicated that three shots were fired".<sup id="cite_ref-WCR3_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCR3-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In 1979, the House Select Committee on Assassinations concluded that there were four shots, one coming from the grassy knoll.<sup id="cite_ref-HSCA_Report_0048a_pp._65-75_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSCA_Report_0048a_pp._65-75-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nationalarch_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalarch-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Warren Commission, and later the House Select Committee on Assassinations, concluded that one of the shots hit President Kennedy in "the back of his neck", exited his throat, and struck Governor Connally in the back, exited the Governor's chest, shattered his right wrist, and implanted itself in his left thigh.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> This conclusion became known as the "<a href="/wiki/Single_bullet_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Single bullet theory">single bullet theory</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Chapter_I,_Section_A197944_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Chapter_I,_Section_A197944-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mary_Moorman" title="Mary Moorman">Mary Moorman</a> said in a TV interview that immediately after the assassination, there were either three or four shots close together, that shots were still being fired after the fatal head shot, and that she was in the line of fire.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In 1967, <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Thompson" title="Josiah Thompson">Josiah Thompson</a> concluded from a close study of the Zapruder film and other forensic evidence, corroborated by the eyewitnesses, that four shots were fired in Dealey Plaza, with one wounding Connally and three hitting Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the day of the assassination, <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Connally" title="Nellie Connally">Nellie Connally</a> was seated in the presidential car next to Governor Connally, who was her husband. In her book <i>From Love Field: Our Final Hours</i>, she said she believed that her husband was hit by a bullet separate from the two that hit Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_of_the_shots">Origin of the shots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Origin of the shots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg/220px-JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg/330px-JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg/440px-JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The wooden fence on the grassy knoll, where many conspiracy theorists believe another gunman stood.</div></div></div>
<p>The Warren Commission concluded that all of the shots fired at President Kennedy came from the sixth-floor window at the southeast corner of the Texas School Book Depository. The Commission based its conclusion on the "cumulative evidence of eyewitnesses, firearms and ballistic experts and medical authorities", including onsite testing, as well as analysis of films and photographs conducted by the FBI and the US Secret Service.<sup id="cite_ref-WCR3_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCR3-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1979, the House Select Committee on Assassinations agreed to publish a report from Warren Commission critic <a href="/wiki/Robert_Groden" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Groden">Robert Groden</a>, in which he named "nearly [two] dozen suspected firing points in Dealey Plaza".<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-VI_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-VI-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> These sites included multiple locations in or on the roof of the Texas School Book Depository, the Dal-Tex Building, the Dallas County Records Building, the triple overpass, a storm drain located along the north curb of Elm Street, and the Grassy Knoll.<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-VI_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-VI-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Josiah Thompson concluded that the shots fired at the motorcade came from three locations: the Texas School Book Depository, the Grassy Knoll, and the Dal-Tex Building.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Testimony_of_eyewitnesses">Testimony of eyewitnesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Testimony of eyewitnesses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to some assassination researchers, the grassy knoll was identified by most witnesses as the area from where shots were fired.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs198988_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs198988-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feldman_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
