In March 1965, Harold Feldman wrote that there were 121 witnesses to the assassination listed in the Warren Report, 51 of whom indicated that the shots that killed Kennedy came from the grassy knoll, while 32 said the shots originated from the Texas School Book Depository.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> In 1967, Josiah Thompson examined the statements of 64 witnesses and concluded that 33 of them thought that the shots emanated from the grassy knoll.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007847_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007847-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1966, <i><a href="/wiki/Esquire_(magazine)" title="Esquire (magazine)">Esquire</a></i> magazine credited Feldman with "advanc[ing] the theory that there were two assassins: one on the grassy knoll and one in the Book Depository".<sup id="cite_ref-Esquire_1966_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire_1966-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Jim Marrs also wrote that the weight of evidence suggested shots came from both the grassy knoll and the Texas School Book Depository.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs198988_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs198988-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Lee_Bowers" title="Lee Bowers">Lee Bowers</a> operated a railroad tower that overlooked the parking lot on the north side of the grassy knoll. He reported that he saw two men behind the grassy knoll's stockyard fence before the shooting took place. The men did not appear to be acting together or doing anything suspicious. After the shooting, Bowers said that one of the men remained behind the fence and lost track of the second man whose clothing blended into the foliage. When interviewed by Mark Lane, Bowers noted that he saw something that attracted his attention, either a flash of light or smoke from the knoll, allowing him to believe "something out of the ordinary" had occurred there. Bowers told Lane that he heard three shots, the last two in quick succession. He stated that there was no way they could have been fired from the same exact rifle.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Bowers later purportedly said to his supervisor, Olan Degaugh, that he saw a man in the parking lot throw what looked like a rifle into one the cars.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> However, in that same 1966 interview, Bowers clarified that the two men he saw were standing in the opening between the pergola and the fence, and that "no one" was behind the fence once the shots were fired.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newman_Family.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Newman_Family.jpg/220px-Newman_Family.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Newman_Family.jpg/330px-Newman_Family.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Newman_Family.jpg/440px-Newman_Family.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1154" data-file-height="1130" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newman_Family.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bill and Gayle Newman drop to the grass and cover their children. The Newmans said that they thought the fatal shot came from behind them.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Jesse Price was the building engineer for the Terminal Annex Building, which is located across from the Texas School Book Depository on the opposite side of Dealey Plaza. He viewed the presidential motorcade from the Terminal Annex Building's roof. In an interview with Mark Lane, Price said that he believed the shots came from "just behind the picket fence where it joins the [triple] underpass".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs198939_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs198939-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_evidence">Physical evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Physical evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several conspiracy theories posit that at least one shooter was located in the <a href="/wiki/Dal-Tex_Building" title="Dal-Tex Building">Dal-Tex Building</a>, located across the street from the <a href="/wiki/Texas_School_Book_Depository" title="Texas School Book Depository">Texas School Book Depository</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Esquire_1967_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire_1967-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/L._Fletcher_Prouty" title="L. Fletcher Prouty">L. Fletcher Prouty</a>, the physical location of <a href="/wiki/James_Tague" title="James Tague">James Tague</a> when he was injured by a bullet fragment is not consistent with the trajectory of a missed shot from the Texas School Book Depository, leading Prouty to theorize that Tague was instead wounded by a missed shot from the second floor of the Dal-Tex Building.<sup id="cite_ref-Prouty_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prouty-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some assassination researchers claim that FBI photographs of the presidential limousine show a bullet hole in its windshield above the rear-view mirror, and a crack in the windshield itself. When Robert Groden, author of <i>The Killing of a President</i>, asked for an explanation, the FBI responded that what Groden thought was a bullet hole "occurred prior to Dallas".<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In 1993, George Whitaker, a manager at the Ford Motor Company's Rouge Plant in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, told attorney and criminal justice professor Doug Weldon that after reporting to work on November 25, 1963, he discovered the presidential limousine in the Rouge Plant's B building with its windshield removed. Whitaker said that the limousine's removed windshield had a through-and-through bullet hole from the front. He said that he was directed by one of Ford's vice presidents to use the windshield as a template to fabricate a new windshield for installation in the limousine. Whitaker also said he was told to destroy the old one.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceD_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceD-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_photographic_evidence">Film and photographic evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Film and photographic evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Film and photographic evidence of the assassination have led viewers to different conclusions regarding the origin of the shots. When the fatal shot was fired, the President's head and upper torso moved backwards — indicating, to many observers, a shot from the right front. Sherry Gutierrez, a certified crime scene and bloodstain pattern analyst, concluded that "the [fatal] head injury to President Kennedy was the result of a single gunshot fired from the right front of the President."<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Paul Chambers believes that the fatal head shot is consistent with a high velocity (approx. 1,200&#160;m/s; 4,000&#160;ft/sec) rifle rather than the medium-velocity (600&#160;m/s; 2,000&#160;ft/sec) Mannlicher–Carcano.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Although it has been thought<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> that Zapruder film frames 312 and 313 show Kennedy's head moving forward before moving backwards, that close inspection of the frames show Kennedy's head actually pivoted both forward and downwards; Anthony Marsh claims that it was the deceleration of the car by driver <a href="/wiki/William_Greer" title="William Greer">William Greer</a> that allowed the President's head to move in that direction.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Some, including Josiah Thompson, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Groden" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Groden">Robert Groden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cyril_Wecht" title="Cyril Wecht">Cyril Wecht</a>, state that the film shows that his head was hit by two near-simultaneous bullets: one from the rear and the other from the right front.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007994_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007994-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Simon_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simon-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrajicek11_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrajicek11-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acoustical_evidence">Acoustical evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Acoustical evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1979, the House Select Committee on Assassinations analyzed a <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_assassination_Dictabelt_recording" title="John F. Kennedy assassination Dictabelt recording">Dictabelt recording of the Dallas Police Department radio dispatch transmissions from the day of the assassination</a> to "resolve questions concerning the number, timing, and origin of the shots fired in Dealey Plaza".<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-IB_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-IB-165">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The Committee concluded that the source of the recording was from an open microphone on the motorcycle of Dallas police officer H.B. McLain escorting the motorcade<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Chapter_I,_Section_B197978_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Chapter_I,_Section_B197978-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> and that "the scientific acoustical evidence established a high probability that two gunmen fired at President John F. Kennedy."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Chapter_I,_Section_B197993_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations_of_the_U.S._House_of_Representatives,_Chapter_I,_Section_B197993-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, the acoustical analysis that the HSCA presented as evidence for two gunmen has since been discredited.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007377_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007377-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Campbell2008_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell2008-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ATY_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATY-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48_years_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48_years-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Knight2007_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight2007-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Olmsted2011_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olmsted2011-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The HSCA acoustic experts said the Dictabelt evidence came from police officer McLain.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> However, McLain stated that he was not yet in Dealey Plaza when the assassination occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> A skeptical McLain asked the Committee, "If it was my radio on my motorcycle, why did it not record the revving up at high speed plus my siren when we immediately took off for Parkland Hospital?"<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Also, in 1982, a panel of 12 scientists appointed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a>, including Nobel laureates <a href="/wiki/Norman_Ramsey" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Ramsey">Norman Ramsey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Walter_Alvarez" title="Luis Walter Alvarez">Luis Alvarez</a>, unanimously concluded that the HSCA's acoustic evidence was "seriously flawed". They concluded that the recording was made after the President had already been shot and that the recording did not indicate any additional gunshots.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>  Their conclusions were later published in the journal <i><a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 2001 article in <i><a href="/wiki/Science_%26_Justice" title="Science &amp; Justice">Science &amp; Justice</a></i>, a publication of Britain's Forensic Science Society, D.B. Thomas wrote that the NAS investigation was itself flawed. Thomas analyzed audio recordings made during the assassination and concluded with a 96% certainty that a shot was fired from the Grassy Knoll in front of and to the right of the President's limousine.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mirror_of_missing_story_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mirror_of_missing_story-175">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, Thomas's conclusions were rebutted in the same journal. Ralph Linsker and several members of the original NAS team reanalyzed the recordings and reaffirmed the earlier conclusion of the NAS report that the alleged shot sounds were recorded approximately one minute after the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> In a 2010 book, D.B. Thomas challenged the 2005 <i>Science &amp; Justice</i> article and restated his conclusion that there actually were two gunmen.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_evidence">Medical evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Medical evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some researchers have pointed to the large number of doctors and nurses at <a href="/wiki/Parkland_Memorial_Hospital" title="Parkland Memorial Hospital">Parkland Memorial Hospital</a> who reported that a major portion of the back of the President's head was blown out.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers201331-_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers201331--136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs198955–89_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs198955–89-180">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In 1979, the HSCA noted: "The various accounts of the nature of the wounds to the President ... as described by the staff at Parkland Memorial Hospital, differed from those in the [ <a href="/wiki/Bethesda_Naval_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Bethesda Naval Hospital">Bethesda</a> ] autopsy report, as well as from what appears in the autopsy photographs and X-rays". The HSCA concluded that the most probable explanation for the discrepancy between the Parkland doctors' testimony and the Bethesda autopsy witnesses was "that the observations of the Parkland doctors [were] incorrect".<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> However, when researcher and <a href="/wiki/Ophthalmologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Ophthalmologist">ophthalmologist</a> Dr. Gary Aquilar, examined the interviews of the Bethesda witnesses, which were declassified in the 1990s, he found that these witnesses also agreed that there was a large, avulsive hole in the rear of Kennedy’s skull, suggesting an exit wound and that Kennedy was hit from the front.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some critics skeptical of the official "<a href="/wiki/Single_bullet_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Single bullet theory">single bullet theory</a>" have stated that the bullet's trajectory, which hit Kennedy above the right shoulder blade and passed through his neck (according to the autopsy), would have had to change course to pass through Connally's rib cage and fracture his wrist.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (March 2012)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Kennedy's death certificate, which was signed by his personal physician Dr. George Burkley, locates the bullet at "about the level of the third <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_vertebra" class="mw-redirect" title="Thoracic vertebra">thoracic vertebra</a>" — which some claim was not high enough to exit his throat.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, since the shooter was in a sixth floor window of the Book Depository building, the bullet traveled downward. The autopsy descriptive sheet displays a diagram of the President's body with the same low placement at the third thoracic vertebra.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The holes in the back of his shirt and jacket are also claimed to support a wound too low to be consistent with the "single bullet theory".<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="photos are insufficient means to support assertion (March 2012)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="photos are insufficient means to support assertion (March 2012)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>There is a conflicting testimony regarding the autopsy performed on Kennedy's body, particularly during the examination on his brain and whether or not the photos submitted as evidence are the same as those taken during the examination.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Douglas Horne, the Assassination Record Review Board's chief analyst for military records, said he was "90 to 95% certain" that the photographs in the <a href="/wiki/National_Archives_and_Records_Administration" title="National Archives and Records Administration">National Archives</a> are not really of Kennedy's brain. Supporting Horne was Dr. Gary Aguilar, who stated, "According to Horne's findings, the second brain — which showed an exit wound in the front — allegedly replaced Kennedy's real brain — which revealed much greater damage to the rear, consistent with an exit wound and thus evidence of a shot from the front."<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Paul O'Connor, a <a href="/wiki/Medical_laboratory_scientist" title="Medical laboratory scientist">laboratory technologist</a> who assisted in the President's autopsy, claimed that the autopsy at <a href="/wiki/Bethesda_Naval_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Bethesda Naval Hospital">Bethesda Naval Hospital</a> was conducted in obedience to a high command<sup id="cite_ref-Douglass_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Douglass-194">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> and that nearly all the brain matter in Kennedy's skull was already missing before the autopsy at Bethesda hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his book <i>JFK and the Unspeakable</i>, James Douglass cites autopsy doctor Pierre Finck's testimony at the <a href="/wiki/Trial_of_Clay_Shaw" title="Trial of Clay Shaw">trial of Clay Shaw</a> as evidence that Finck was "... a reluctant witness to the military control over the doctors' examination of the president's body".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010311–312_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010311–312-197">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A bone fragment found in Dealey Plaza by William Allen Harper the day following the assassination was reported by the HSCA's Forensic Pathology Panel to have been part of Kennedy's <a href="/wiki/Parietal_bone" title="Parietal bone">parietal bone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-VII_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-VII-199">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Some critics of the lone gunman theory, including James Douglass, David Lifton, and David Mantick, state that the fragment is actually a piece of <a href="/wiki/Occipital_bone" title="Occipital bone">occipital bone</a> ejected from an exit wound in the back of Kennedy's head.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010283–284,_461_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010283–284,_461-200">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> They stated this finding is evidence of a cover-up as it proves that the skull radiographs obtained during the autopsy, which do not show significant bone loss in the occipital area, are not authentic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010283–284,_461_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010283–284,_461-200">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Oswald.27s_marksmanship"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Oswald's_marksmanship">Oswald's marksmanship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Oswald&#039;s marksmanship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Warren Commission examined the capabilities of the Carcano rifle and ammunition, as well as Oswald's military training and post-military experience, and determined that Oswald had the ability to fire three shots within a time span of 4.8 to 5.6 seconds.<sup id="cite_ref-WCR4_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCR4-201">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> According to their report, an army specialist using Oswald's rifle was able to duplicate the feat and even improved on the time. The report also states that the Army Infantry Weapons Evaluation Branch test fired Oswald's rifle 47 times and found that it was "quite accurate", comparing it to the accuracy of an <a href="/wiki/M14_rifle" title="M14 rifle">M14 rifle</a>. Also contained in the Commission report is testimony by <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Corps">Marine Corps</a> Major Eugene Anderson confirming that Oswald's military records show that he qualified as "<a href="/wiki/Sharpshooter" title="Sharpshooter">sharpshooter</a>" in 1956.
</p><p>According to official <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Corps">Marine Corps</a> records, Oswald was tested in shooting in December 1956, scoring 212 (slightly above the minimum for qualification as a sharpshooter — the intermediate category), but in May 1959, he scored 191 (earning the lower designation of marksman).<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> The highest marksmanship category in the Marine Corps is 'Expert' (220).<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite Oswald's confirmed marksmanship in the USMC, conspiracy theorists like Walt Brown and authors such as <a href="/wiki/Richard_H._Popkin" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard H. Popkin">Richard H. Popkin</a> contend that Oswald was a notoriously poor shot, that his rifle was inaccurate, and that no reconstruction of the event has ever been able to duplicate his ability to fire three shots within the time frame given by the Warren Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-Aaronovitch2010_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aaronovitch2010-204">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007xxxviii_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007xxxviii-205">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_of_Oswald">Role of Oswald</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Role of Oswald">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Warren Commission and other federal investigations ruled that Oswald either acted alone or conspired with others in the assassination, citing his actions in the years leading up to the event. Evidence of Oswald's pro-communist and radical tendencies include his defection to Russia, the New Orleans branch of the <a href="/wiki/Fair_Play_for_Cuba_Committee" title="Fair Play for Cuba Committee">Fair Play for Cuba Committee</a> he had organized, and also various public and private statements made by him espousing Marxism and other leftist ideologies. Others have argued that his behavior was in fact a carefully planned ruse as part of an effort by U.S. intelligence agencies to infiltrate subversive groups and conduct counter-intelligence operations in communist countries, and that his role in the assassination was that of either an agent or an informant of the government trying to expose the plot behind the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-WCReport_0342b_p._660_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCReport_0342b_p._660-206">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBroderickMiller2008206–207_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBroderickMiller2008206–207-207">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989189–196,_226–235_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989189–196,_226–235-208">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Goldman_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldman-209">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oswald himself claimed to be innocent, denying all charges and even declaring to reporters that he was "just a <a href="/wiki/Fall_guy" title="Fall guy">patsy</a>". He also insisted that the photos of him holding a rifle had been faked, an assertion contradicted by statements made by his wife, Marina, and the analysis of photographic experts such as Lyndal L. Shaneyfelt of the FBI.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Oswald's role as FBI informant was investigated by Lee Rankin and others of the Warren Commission, but their findings were inconclusive. Several FBI employees had made statements indicating that Oswald was indeed a paid informant, but the commission was nonetheless unable to verify the veracity of those claims.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> FBI agent <a href="/wiki/James_Hosty" class="mw-redirect" title="James Hosty">James P. Hosty</a> reported that his office's interactions with Oswald were limited to dealing with his complaints about being harassed by the Bureau for being a communist sympathizer. In the weeks before the assassination, Oswald made a personal visit to the FBI's Dallas branch office with a hand-delivered letter which purportedly contained a threat of some sort but, controversially, Hosty destroyed the letter by order of J. Gordon Shanklin, his supervisor.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some researchers suggest that Oswald served as an active agent of the Central Intelligence Agency, often pointing to how he attempted to defect to Russia but was, however, able to return without difficulty (even receiving a repatriation loan from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">State Department</a><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>) as evidence of such. A former roommate of Oswald, James Botelho (who would later become a California judge) stated in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lane_(author)" title="Mark Lane (author)">Mark Lane</a> that he believed Oswald was involved in an intelligence assignment in Russia,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989110–111_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989110–111-217">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglass201040_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglass201040-218">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> although Botelho did not mention any of those suspicions in his testimony to the Warren Commission years earlier. Oswald's mother, Marguerite, often insisted that her son was recruited by an agency of the U.S. Government and sent to Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-WCReport_0342b_p._660_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCReport_0342b_p._660-206">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> New Orleans District Attorney (and later judge) <a href="/wiki/Jim_Garrison" title="Jim Garrison">Jim Garrison</a>, who in 1967 brought <a href="/wiki/Clay_Shaw" title="Clay Shaw">Clay Shaw</a> to <a href="/wiki/Trial_of_Clay_Shaw" title="Trial of Clay Shaw">trial for the assassination of President Kennedy</a>, also held the opinion that Oswald was most likely a CIA agent drawn into the plot to be used as a scapegoat, even going as far as to say that Oswald "genuinely was probably a hero".<sup id="cite_ref-Turner,_Nigel_1991_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner,_Nigel_1991-219">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Senator Richard Schweiker, a member of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Senate_Select_Committee_on_Intelligence" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Senate Select Committee on Intelligence">U.S. Senate Select Committee on Intelligence</a> remarked that "everywhere you look with [Oswald], there're fingerprints of intelligence".<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Sprague" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Sprague">Richard Sprague</a>, interim staff director and chief counsel to the <a href="/wiki/U.S._House_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. House Select Committee on Assassinations">U.S. House Select Committee on Assassinations</a>, stated that if he "had to do it over again", he would have investigated the Kennedy assassination by probing Oswald's ties to the Central Intelligence Agency.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> In 1978, former CIA paymaster and accountant James Wilcott testified before the <a href="/wiki/HSCA" class="mw-redirect" title="HSCA">HSCA</a>, stating that Lee Harvey Oswald was a "known agent" of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> Wilcott and his wife, Elsie (also a former employee of the CIA) later repeated those claims in an article in the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> Despite its official policy of neither confirming nor denying the status of agents, both the CIA itself and many officers working in the region at the time (including <a href="/wiki/David_Atlee_Phillips" title="David Atlee Phillips">David Atlee Phillips</a>) have "unofficially" dismissed the plausibility of any possible ties to Oswald and the agency. <a href="/wiki/G._Robert_Blakey" title="G. Robert Blakey">Robert Blakey</a>, staff director and chief counsel for the U.S. House Select Committee on Assassinations, supported that assessment in his conclusions as well.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_gunmen">Alternative gunmen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Alternative gunmen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition to Oswald, Jerome Kroth has named 26 people as "Possible Assassins In Dealey Plaza".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> They include: <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Bosch" title="Orlando Bosch">Orlando Bosch</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Files" title="James Files">James Files</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Fishel_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fishel-226">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Fitzgerald_(CIA_officer)" title="Desmond Fitzgerald (CIA officer)">Desmond Fitzgerald</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Harrelson" title="Charles Harrelson">Charles Harrelson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFishel2005309–312_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFishel2005309–312-227">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Hemming" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerry Hemming">Gerry Hemming</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chauncey_Holt" class="mw-redirect" title="Chauncey Holt">Chauncey Holt</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hunt" class="mw-redirect" title="Howard Hunt">Howard Hunt</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Nicoletti" title="Charles Nicoletti">Charles Nicoletti</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFishel2005309–312_227-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFishel2005309–312-227">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rogers_(murder_suspect)" title="Charles Rogers (murder suspect)">Charles Rogers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Roselli" class="mw-redirect" title="Johnny Roselli">Johnny Roselli</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lucien_Sarti" title="Lucien Sarti">Lucien Sarti</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFishel2005309–312_227-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFishel2005309–312-227">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sturgis" title="Frank Sturgis">Frank Sturgis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195_225-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKroth2003195-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Three_tramps">Three tramps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Three tramps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Three_tramps" title="Three tramps">Three tramps</a></div> <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Three_Tramps.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_Three_Tramps.jpg/220px-The_Three_Tramps.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_Three_Tramps.jpg/330px-The_Three_Tramps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_Three_Tramps.jpg/440px-The_Three_Tramps.jpg 2x" data-file-width="986" data-file-height="682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Three_Tramps.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Three Tramps</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Vincent_Bugliosi" title="Vincent Bugliosi">Vincent Bugliosi</a> provides a "partial list of assassins ... whom one or more conspiracy theorists have actually named and identified as having fired a weapon at Kennedy" in his book <i><a href="/wiki/Reclaiming_History" title="Reclaiming History">Reclaiming History</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> He also mentions the <a href="/wiki/Three_tramps" title="Three tramps">three tramps</a>, men photographed by several <a href="/wiki/Newspapers_of_Dallas,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Newspapers of Dallas, Texas">Dallas-area newspapers</a> under police escort near the Texas School Book Depository shortly after the assassination. Since the mid-1960s, various allegations have been made about the identities of the men and their involvement in a conspiracy to kill Kennedy. Records released by the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Police_Department" title="Dallas Police Department">Dallas Police Department</a> in 1989 identified the men as Gus Abrams, Harold Doyle, and John Gedney.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007933_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007933-229">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_other_conspirators">Allegations of other conspirators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Allegations of other conspirators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="E._Howard_Hunt">E. Howard Hunt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: E. Howard Hunt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/E_Howard_Hunt#JFK_conspiracy_allegations" class="mw-redirect" title="E Howard Hunt">E Howard Hunt §&#160;JFK conspiracy allegations</a></div>
<p>The theory that former CIA agent and <a href="/wiki/Watergate_scandal" title="Watergate scandal">Watergate</a> burglar <a href="/wiki/E._Howard_Hunt" title="E. Howard Hunt">E. Howard Hunt</a> was a participant in the assassination of Kennedy garnered much publicity from 1978 to 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-Trahair_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trahair-230">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> In 1981, he won a libel judgment against <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Lobby" title="Liberty Lobby">Liberty Lobby</a>'s paper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spotlight" title="The Spotlight">The Spotlight</a></i>, which in 1978 printed an allegation by <a href="/wiki/Victor_Marchetti" title="Victor Marchetti">Victor Marchetti</a> suggesting Hunt's involvement in a conspiracy; the libel award was thrown out on appeal and the newspaper was successfully defended by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lane_(author)" title="Mark Lane (author)">Mark Lane</a> in a second trial.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Washington_Post_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Washington_Post-231">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> Former KGB <a href="/wiki/Archivist" title="Archivist">archivist</a> <a href="/wiki/Vasili_Mitrokhin" title="Vasili Mitrokhin">Vasili Mitrokhin</a> indicated in 1999 that Hunt was made part of a fabricated conspiracy theory disseminated by a Soviet "<a href="/wiki/Active_measures" title="Active measures">active measures</a>" program designed to discredit the CIA and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Andrew_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andrew-232">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrahair2009188-190_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrahair2009188-190-233">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> After his death in 2007, an audio-taped "<a href="/wiki/Deathbed_confession" title="Deathbed confession">deathbed confession</a>" in which Hunt claimed first-hand knowledge of a conspiracy, as a co-conspirator, was released by his son Saint John Hunt.<sup id="cite_ref-Hedegaard_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hedegaard-234">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> In the confession, Hunt claimed to have been a "bench warmer" in Dallas during the events, and he named several high-level CIA operatives as those who likely carried out the logistics of the assassination. Hunt named Vice President Lyndon Johnson as the most likely figure behind the main impetus of the conspiracy.<sup id="cite_ref-Hedegaard_234-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hedegaard-234">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> The authenticity of the confession was met with some skepticism.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-Trahair_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trahair-230">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Williams_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-235">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Timothy_W._Maier_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timothy_W._Maier-236">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="J._D._Tippit">J. D. Tippit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: J. D. Tippit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dallas Police Officer <a href="/wiki/J._D._Tippit" title="J. D. Tippit">J. D. Tippit</a> has been named in some conspiracy theories as a renegade CIA operative sent to silence Oswald<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerry2003391_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerry2003391-237">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Barry_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barry-238">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> and as the "<a href="/wiki/Badge_man" class="mw-redirect" title="Badge man">badge man</a>" assassin on the grassy knoll.<sup id="cite_ref-Barry_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barry-238">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> According to some Warren Commission critics, Oswald was set up to be killed by Tippit, but Tippit was killed by Oswald before he could carry out his assignment.<sup id="cite_ref-Bonokowski_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonokowski-239">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Other critics doubt that Tippit was killed by Oswald and assert he was shot by other conspirators.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerry2003391_237-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerry2003391-237">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bonokowski_239-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonokowski-239">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> (See <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories#Unnamed_accomplice(s)_in_the_murder_of_J._D._Tippit" title="John F. Kennedy assassination conspiracy theories">section below</a>.) Some critics have alleged that Tippit was associated with organized crime or <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">right-wing politics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerry2003391_237-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerry2003391-237">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bernard_Weissman">Bernard Weissman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Bernard Weissman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Welcome_mr_kennedy_to_dallas_small.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e5/Welcome_mr_kennedy_to_dallas_small.jpg/200px-Welcome_mr_kennedy_to_dallas_small.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="307" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/e5/Welcome_mr_kennedy_to_dallas_small.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="254" data-file-height="390" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Welcome_mr_kennedy_to_dallas_small.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Advertisement in the November 22, 1963, <i>Dallas Morning News</i>, placed by Bernard Weissman and three others.</div></div></div>
<p>According to the Warren Commission, the publication of a full-page, paid advertisement critical of Kennedy in the November 22, 1963, <i>Dallas Morning News</i>, which was signed by "The American Fact-Finding Committee" and noted Bernard Weissman as its chairman, was investigated to determine whether any members of the group claiming responsibility for it were connected to Oswald or to the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964293–299_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964293–299-240">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> The Commission stated that "The American Fact-Finding Committee" was a fictitious sponsoring organization and that there was no evidence linking the four men responsible for the genesis of the ad with either Oswald or Ruby, or to a conspiracy to assassinate Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964293–299_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964293–299-240">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Related to the advertisement, Mark Lane testified during the Warren Commission's hearings that an informant whom he refused to name told him that Weismann had met with Tippit and Ruby eight days before the assassination at Ruby's Carousel Club.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964293–299_240-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964293–299-240">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> The Commission reported that they "found no evidence that such a meeting took place anywhere at any time"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964298_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964298-241">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> and that there was no "credible evidence that any of the three men knew each other".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Appendix_121964663_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Appendix_121964663-242">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lane later stated that he initially learned of the meeting through reporter Thayer Waldo of the <i><a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth_Star-Telegram" title="Fort Worth Star-Telegram">Fort Worth Star-Telegram</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Playboy;_February,_1967_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playboy;_February,_1967-243">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> According to Lane, a "prominent Dallas figure" who frequented Ruby's Carousel Club told Waldo, and later Lane, that he observed the meeting of the three men at the club.<sup id="cite_ref-Playboy;_February,_1967_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playboy;_February,_1967-243">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> He said, "I had promised the man he would not be involved; he was a leading Dallas citizen; he was married, and the stripper he was going with had become pregnant."<sup id="cite_ref-Playboy;_February,_1967_243-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playboy;_February,_1967-243">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Despite not having revealed to the Warren Commission that Waldo was his original source of the alleged meeting, Lane disputed their findings and complained that they failed to ask Waldo about it.<sup id="cite_ref-Gavzer_&amp;_Moody_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gavzer_&amp;_Moody-244">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Aynesworth" title="Hugh Aynesworth">Hugh Aynesworth</a>, the source of the allegation whose identity Lane promised not to reveal was Carroll Jarnagin,<sup id="cite_ref-Aynesworth_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aynesworth-245">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> a Dallas attorney who had also claimed to have overheard a meeting between Oswald and Ruby.<sup id="cite_ref-Eaton_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eaton-246">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> Aynesworth wrote: "Several people in Dallas were well aware of Jarnagin's tale, and that he later admitted making it all up."<sup id="cite_ref-Aynesworth_245-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aynesworth-245">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Unnamed_accomplice.28s.29_in_the_murder_of_J._D._Tippit"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Unnamed_accomplice(s)_in_the_murder_of_J._D._Tippit">Unnamed accomplice(s) in the murder of J. D. Tippit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Unnamed accomplice(s) in the murder of J. D. Tippit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Warren Commission concluded that Oswald "killed Dallas Police Officer <a href="/wiki/J._D._Tippit" title="J. D. Tippit">J. D. Tippit</a> in an apparent attempt to escape."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964195_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964195-247">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> The evidence that formed the basis for this conclusion was: "(1) two eyewitnesses who heard the shots and saw the shooting of Dallas Police Patrolman J. D. Tippit and seven eyewitnesses who saw the flight of the gunman with revolver in hand positively identified Lee Harvey Oswald as the man they saw fire the shots or flee from the scene, (2) the cartridge cases found near the scene of the shooting were fired from the revolver in the possession of Oswald at the time of his arrest, to the exclusion of all other weapons, (3) the revolver in Oswald's possession at the time of his arrest was purchased by and belonged to Oswald, and (4) Oswald's jacket was found along the path of flight taken by the gunman as he fled from the scene of the killing."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964176_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964176-248">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some researchers have alleged that the murder of Officer Tippit was part of a conspiracy to kill President Kennedy. Jim Marrs hypothesized that "the slaying of Officer J. D. Tippit may have played some part in [a] scheme to have Oswald killed, perhaps to eliminate co-conspirator Tippit or simply to anger Dallas police and cause itchy trigger fingers."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989585_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989585-249">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> Researcher James Douglass said that "... the killing of [Tippit] helped motivate the Dallas police to kill an armed Oswald in the Texas Theater, which would have disposed of the scapegoat before he could protest his being framed."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010287_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010287-250">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Harold Weisberg offered a simpler explanation: "Immediately, the [flimsy] police case [against Oswald] required a willingness to believe. This was proved by affixing to Oswald the opprobrious epithet of 'cop-killer.'"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010287_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010287-250">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jim_Garrison" title="Jim Garrison">Jim Garrison</a> alleged that evidence was altered to frame Oswald, stating: "If Oswald was innocent of the Tippit murder the foundation of the government's case against him collapsed."<sup id="cite_ref-Garrison_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garrison-251">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some critics doubt that Tippit was killed by Oswald and assert he was shot by other conspirators.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerry2003391_237-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerry2003391-237">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bonokowski_239-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonokowski-239">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> They allege discrepancies in witness testimony and physical evidence that they think call into question the Commission's conclusions regarding the murder of Tippit. According to Jim Marrs, Oswald's guilt in the assassination of Kennedy is placed in question by the presence of "a growing body of evidence to suggest that [he] did not kill Tippit".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989340_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989340-252">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Others say that multiple men were directly involved in Tippit's killing. Conspiracy researcher <a href="/wiki/Kenn_Thomas" title="Kenn Thomas">Kenn Thomas</a> has alleged that the Warren Commission omitted testimony and evidence that two men shot Tippit and that one left the scene in a car.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-253">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>William Alexander — the Dallas assistant district attorney who recommended that Oswald be charged with the Kennedy and Tippit murders — later became skeptical of the Warren Commission's version of the Tippit murder. He stated that the Commission's conclusions on Oswald's movements "don't add up", and that "certainly [Oswald] may have had accomplices."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers2013108_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers2013108-254">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Brian_McKenna" title="Brian McKenna">Brian McKenna</a>'s review of Henry Hurt's book, <i>Reasonable Doubt</i>, Hurt reported that "Tippit may have been killed because he impregnated the wife of another man" and that Dallas police officers lied and altered evidence to set up Oswald to save Tippit's reputation.<sup id="cite_ref-McKenna_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKenna-255">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_regarding_witness_testimony_and_physical_evidence">Allegations regarding witness testimony and physical evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Allegations regarding witness testimony and physical evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Warren Commission identified Helen Markham and Domingo Benavides as two witnesses who actually saw the shooting.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964166–167_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964166–167-256">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> Conspiracy theorist <a href="/wiki/Richard_Belzer" title="Richard Belzer">Richard Belzer</a> criticized the Commission for, in his description, "relying" on the testimony of Markham whom he described as "imaginative".<sup id="cite_ref-Belzer_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belzer-257">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Jim Marrs also took issue with Markham's testimony, stating that her "credibility ... was strained to the breaking point".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989340_252-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989340-252">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Joseph Ball, senior counsel to the Commission, referred to Markham's testimony as "full of mistakes", characterizing her as an "utter screwball".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers2013104–105_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers2013104–105-258">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> The Warren Commission addressed concerns regarding Markham's reliability as a witness and concluded: "However, even in the absence of Mrs. Markham's testimony, there is ample evidence to identify Oswald as the killer of Tippit."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964166–167_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964166–167-256">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Domingo Benavides initially said that he did not think he could identify Tippit's assailant and was never asked to view a police lineup,<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> even though he was the person closest to the killing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989341_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989341-260">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Benavides later testified that the killer resembled pictures he had seen of Oswald.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> Other witnesses were taken to police lineups. However, critics have questioned these lineups as they consisted of people who looked very different from Oswald.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989341_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989341-260">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Additionally, witnesses who did not appear before the Commission identified an assailant who was not Oswald. Acquilla Clemons said she saw two men near Tippit's car just before the shooting.<sup id="cite_ref-Turner,_Nigel_1991_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner,_Nigel_1991-219">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> She said that after the shooting, she ran outside of her house and saw a man with a gun whom she described as "kind of heavy". She said he waved to the second man, urging him to "go on".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers2013105–106_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers2013105–106-263">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> Frank Wright said he emerged from his home and observed the scene seconds after the shooting. He described a man standing by Tippit's body who had on a long coat and said the man ran to a parked car and drove away.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989342_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989342-264">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers2013106_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers2013106-265">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Critics have questioned whether the cartridge cases recovered from the scene were the same as those that were subsequently entered into evidence. Two of the cases were recovered by witness Domingo Benavides and turned over to police officer J.&#160;M. Poe. Poe told the FBI that he marked the shells with his own initials, "J.M.P." to identify them.<sup id="cite_ref-Commission_Exhibit_No._2011_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commission_Exhibit_No._2011-266">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> Sergeant Gerald Hill later testified to the Warren Commission that it was he who had ordered police officer Poe to mark the shells.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> However, Poe's initials were not found on the shells produced by the FBI six months later.<sup id="cite_ref-Commission_Exhibit_No._2011_266-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commission_Exhibit_No._2011-266">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989343_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989343-268">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> Testifying before the Warren Commission, Poe said that although he recalled marking the cases, he "couldn't swear to it".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989343_268-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989343-268">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> The identification of the cases at the crime scene raises more questions. Sergeant Gerald Hill examined one of the shells and radioed the police dispatcher, saying: "The shell at the scene indicates that the suspect is armed with an automatic .38 rather than a pistol."<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> However, Oswald was reportedly arrested carrying a <i>non</i>-automatic .38 Special revolver.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989342_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989342-264">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers201365_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers201365-271">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_regarding_timeline">Allegations regarding timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Allegations regarding timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Warren Commission investigated Oswald's movements between the time of the assassination and the shooting of Tippit, to ascertain whether Oswald might have had an accomplice who helped him flee the Book Depository. The Commission concluded "... through the testimony of seven witnesses [that] Oswald was always alone."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964252_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964252-272">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> According to their final report, Oswald was seen by his housekeeper leaving his rooming house shortly after 1:00&#160;pm and had enough time to travel nine-tenths of a mile (1.4&#160;km) to the scene where Tippit was killed at 1:16&#160;pm.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964254_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964254-273">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Appendix_121964648_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Appendix_121964648-274">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some Warren Commission critics believe that Oswald did not have enough time to get from his house to the scene where Tippit was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerry2003391_237-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerry2003391-237">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> The Commission's own test and estimation of Oswald's walking speed demonstrated that one of the longer routes to the Tippit shooting scene took 17 minutes and 45 seconds to walk.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> No witness ever surfaced who saw Oswald walk from his rooming house to the murder scene.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGroden1995137_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGroden1995137-278">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Conspiracy researcher Robert Groden believes that Tippit's murder may have occurred earlier than the time given in the Warren Report. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGroden1995134–137_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGroden1995134–137-279">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> He notes that the Commission established the time of the shooting as 1:16&#160;pm from police tapes that logged Domingo Benavides's use of the radio in Tippit's car.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964165_275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964165-275">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> However, Benavides testified that he did not approach the car until "a few minutes" after the shooting, because he was afraid that the gunman might return.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> He was assisted in using the radio by witness T. F. Bowley who testified to Dallas police that at the time he arrived to help, "several people were at the scene", and that the time was 1:10&#160;pm.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Witness Helen Markham stated in her affidavit to the Dallas Sheriff's department that Tippit was killed at "approximately 1:06 pm."<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> She later affirmed the time in testimony before the Warren Commission, saying: "I wouldn't be afraid to bet it wasn't 6 or 7 minutes after 1."<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGroden1995136_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGroden1995136-284">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> She initially told the FBI that the shooting occurred "possibly around 1:30&#160;pm."<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> In an unpublished manuscript titled <i>When They Kill a President</i>, Deputy Sheriff Roger Craig stated that when he heard the news that Tippit had been shot, he noted that the time was 1:06&#160;pm.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> However, in a later statement to the press, Craig seemed confused about the time of the shooting.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Warren "Butch" Burroughs, who ran the concession stand at the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Texas Theater">Texas Theater</a> where Oswald was arrested, said that Oswald came into the theater between 1:00 and 1:07&#160;pm; he also claimed he sold Oswald popcorn at 1:15&#160;p.m. — the "official" time of Officer Tippit's murder.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010290,_466_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglass2010290,_466-288">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> Julia Postal told the Warren Commission that Burroughs initially told her the same thing, although when she later discussed the event with him, she became skeptical about his version.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> A theatre patron, Jack Davis, also corroborated Burroughs's time, claiming he observed Oswald in the theatre prior to 1:20 pm.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989353_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989353-291">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Unidentified_witnesses">Unidentified witnesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Unidentified witnesses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Umbrella_Man.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Umbrella_Man.jpg/250px-Umbrella_Man.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Umbrella_Man.jpg/375px-Umbrella_Man.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Umbrella_Man.jpg/500px-Umbrella_Man.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1581" data-file-height="1178" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Umbrella_Man.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Following the assassination of President Kennedy the "umbrella man" can be seen sitting on the sidewalk next to the "dark complected man" on the right side of the photograph.</div></div></div>
<p>Some conspiracy theories surrounding the Kennedy assassination have focused on witnesses to the assassination who have not been identified, or who have not identified themselves, despite the media attention that the Kennedy assassination has received.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Umbrella_man">Umbrella man</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Umbrella man">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Umbrella_Man_(JFK_assassination)" class="mw-redirect" title="Umbrella Man (JFK assassination)">Umbrella Man (JFK assassination)</a></div>
<p>The so-called "umbrella man" was one of the closest bystanders to the president when he was first struck by a bullet. The "umbrella man" has become the subject of conspiracy theories after footage of the assassination showed him holding an open umbrella as the Kennedy motorcade passed, despite the fact that it was not raining at the time. One conspiracy theory, proposed by assassination researcher Robert Cutler, suggests that a dart with a paralyzing agent could have been fired from the umbrella, disabling Kennedy and making him a "sitting duck" for an assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> (In 1975, CIA weapons developer Charles Senseney told the <a href="/wiki/Senate_Intelligence_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate Intelligence Committee">Senate Intelligence Committee</a> that such an umbrella weapon was in the hands of the CIA in 1963.)<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> A more prevalent conspiracy theory holds that the umbrella could have been used to provide visual signals to hidden gunmen.<sup id="cite_ref-Marrs,_Jim_1989_pp._29-33_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marrs,_Jim_1989_pp._29-33-294">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1978, Louie Steven Witt came forward and identified himself as the "umbrella man". Testifying before the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations" title="United States House Select Committee on Assassinations">United States House Select Committee on Assassinations</a>, Witt stated he brought the umbrella to heckle Kennedy and protest the <a href="/wiki/Appeasement" title="Appeasement">appeasement</a> policies of the president's father, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kennedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Kennedy">Joseph Kennedy</a>. He added: "I think if the <i>Guinness Book of World Records</i> had a category for people who were at the wrong place at the wrong time, doing the wrong thing, I would be No. 1 in that position, without even a close runner-up."<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> Some researchers have noted a number of inconsistencies with Witt's story, however, and do not believe him to be the true "umbrella man".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs198930_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs198930-296">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The "umbrella man" is the subject of a 2011 documentary short by <a href="/wiki/Errol_Morris" title="Errol Morris">Errol Morris</a>, for <i>The New York Times</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dark_complected_man">Dark complected man</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Dark complected man">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An unidentified individual who is referred to by some conspiracy theorists as the "dark complected man" can be seen in several photographs, taken seconds after the assassination, sitting on the sidewalk next to the "umbrella man" on the north side of Elm Street. Louie Steven Witt, who identified himself as the "umbrella man", said he was unable to identify the other individual, whose dark complexion has led some conspiracy theorists to speculate Cuban government involvement, or Cuban exile involvement, in the assassination of Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-Marrs,_Jim_1989_pp._29-33_294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marrs,_Jim_1989_pp._29-33-294">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_witnesses">Possible witnesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Possible witnesses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some conspiracy theories focus on individuals that it is claimed can be seen in photographs of the assassination. Both "badge man" and "black dog man" have been suggested as possible assassins of President Kennedy.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Badge_man">Badge man</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Badge man">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Badge_Man" title="Badge Man">Badge Man</a></div>
