</p><p>In September 1976, <a href="/wiki/George_de_Mohrenschildt" title="George de Mohrenschildt">George de Mohrenschildt</a>, a petroleum geologist and a friend of both Bush and Oswald,<sup id="cite_ref-431" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-431">&#91;428&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-library54_432-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-library54-432">&#91;429&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-433" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-433">&#91;430&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers2013172_434-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers2013172-434">&#91;431&#93;</a></sup> wrote a letter to Bush, then director of the CIA, asking for his assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-435" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-435">&#91;432&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-436" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-436">&#91;433&#93;</a></sup> According to Morley, Mohrenschildt was being pressured by congressional investigators to testify on the assassination, causing him to write the letter in distress. Bush acknowledged that he knew Mohrenschildt but failed to respond to the letter, and Mohrenschildt committed suicide six months later.<sup id="cite_ref-437" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-437">&#91;434&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-438" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-438">&#91;435&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-439" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-439">&#91;436&#93;</a></sup> Morley argues that the letter's existence does not demonstrate guilt for either man, but merely that Bush was uninterested in questioning the CIA's account of the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-stout_430-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stout-430">&#91;427&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuban_government_conspiracy">Cuban government conspiracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Cuban government conspiracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In its report, the Warren Commission stated that it had investigated "dozens of allegations of a conspiratorial contact between Oswald and agents of the Cuban Government" and had found no evidence of Cuban involvement in the assassination of President Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964305,_374_440-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964305,_374-440">&#91;437&#93;</a></sup> The House Select Committee on Assassinations also wrote: "The committee believes, on the basis of the evidence available to it, that the Cuban Government was not involved in the assassination of President Kennedy".<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-IC_339-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-IC-339">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> However, some conspiracy theorists continue to allege that <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> ordered the assassination of Kennedy in retaliation for the CIA's previous attempts to assassinate him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBroderick2008208_385-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBroderick2008208-385">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early 1960s, <a href="/wiki/Clare_Boothe_Luce" title="Clare Boothe Luce">Clare Boothe Luce</a>, wife of <a href="/wiki/Time-Life" class="mw-redirect" title="Time-Life">Time-Life</a> publisher <a href="/wiki/Henry_Luce" title="Henry Luce">Henry Luce</a>, was one of a number of prominent Americans who sponsored anti-Castro groups. This support included funding exiles in commando speedboat raids against Cuba. In 1975, Clare Luce said that on the night of the assassination, she received a call from a member of a commando group she had sponsored. According to Luce, the caller's name was "something like" Julio Fernandez and he claimed he was calling her from New Orleans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers2013392-_441-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers2013392--441">&#91;438&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-442" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-442">&#91;439&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Luce, Fernandez told her that Oswald had approached his group with an offer to help assassinate Castro. Fernandez further claimed that he and his associates eventually found out that Oswald was a communist and supporter of Castro. He said that with this new-found knowledge, his group kept a close watch on Oswald until Oswald suddenly came into money and went to <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> and then Dallas.<sup id="cite_ref-443" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-443">&#91;440&#93;</a></sup> Finally, according to Luce, Fernandez told her, "There is a Cuban Communist assassination team at large and Oswald was their hired gun."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESummers1998323_444-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESummers1998323-444">&#91;441&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Luce said that she told the caller to give his information to the FBI. Subsequently, Luce would reveal the details of the incident to both the <a href="/wiki/Church_Committee" title="Church Committee">Church Committee</a> and the HSCA. Both committees investigated the incident, but were unable to uncover any evidence to corroborate the allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-445" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-445">&#91;442&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 1967, CIA Director <a href="/wiki/Richard_Helms" title="Richard Helms">Richard Helms</a> told President Lyndon Johnson that the CIA had tried to assassinate Castro. Helms further stated that the CIA had employed members of the Mafia in this effort, and "... that CIA plots to assassinate Fidel Castro dated back to August of 1960 — to the Eisenhower Administration." Helms also said that the plots against Castro continued into the Kennedy Administration and that Attorney General Robert Kennedy had known about both the plots and the Mafia's involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-theatlantic.com_446-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theatlantic.com-446">&#91;443&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On separate occasions, Johnson told two prominent television newsmen that he believed that JFK's assassination had been organized by Castro as retaliation for the CIA's efforts to kill Castro. In October 1968, Johnson told veteran newsman <a href="/wiki/Howard_K._Smith" title="Howard K. Smith">Howard K. Smith</a> of <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> that "Kennedy was trying to get to Castro, but Castro got to him first." In September 1969, in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Walter_Cronkite" title="Walter Cronkite">Walter Cronkite</a> of <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a>, Johnson said in regard to the assassination, "[I could not] honestly say that I've ever been completely relieved of the fact that there might have been international connections", and referenced unnamed "others". Finally, in 1971, Johnson told his former speechwriter Leo Janos of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine that he "never believed that Oswald acted alone".<sup id="cite_ref-theatlantic.com_446-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theatlantic.com-446">&#91;443&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1977, Castro was interviewed by newsman <a href="/wiki/Bill_Moyers" title="Bill Moyers">Bill Moyers</a>. Castro denied any involvement in Kennedy's death, saying:
</p>
<blockquote><p>It would have been absolute insanity by Cuba. ... It would have been a provocation. Needless to say, it would have been to run the risk that our country would have been destroyed by the United States. Nobody who's not insane could have thought about [killing Kennedy in retaliation].<sup id="cite_ref-Bill_Moyers_1977_387-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bill_Moyers_1977-387">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989154_447-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989154-447">&#91;444&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_government_conspiracy">Soviet government conspiracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Soviet government conspiracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Warren Commission reported that they found no evidence that the Soviet Union was involved in the assassination of President Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964374_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_61964374-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The House Select Committee on Assassinations also wrote: "The committee believes, on the basis of the evidence available to it, that the Soviet Government was not involved in the assassination of President Kennedy".<sup id="cite_ref-HCSA-IC_339-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCSA-IC-339">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to some conspiracy theorists, the Soviet Union, with <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> motivated by having to back down during the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a>, was responsible for the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBroderick2008208_385-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBroderick2008208-385">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a 1966 FBI document, Colonel Boris Ivanov — chief of the KGB Residency in New York City at the time of the assassination — stated that it was his personal opinion that the assassination had been planned by an organized group, rather than a lone individual. The same document stated, "... officials of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union believed there was some well-organized conspiracy on the part of the 'ultraright' in the United States to effect a '<a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d&#39;état">coup</a>.'"<sup id="cite_ref-448" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-448">&#91;445&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Much later, the high-ranking <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Soviet Bloc</a> intelligence defector, Lt. Gen. <a href="/wiki/Ion_Mihai_Pacepa" title="Ion Mihai Pacepa">Ion Mihai Pacepa</a>, said that he had a conversation with <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Ceau%C5%9Fescu" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicolae Ceauşescu">Nicolae Ceauşescu</a> who told him about "ten international leaders the <a href="/wiki/Kremlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Kremlin">Kremlin</a> killed or tried to kill", including Kennedy. He claimed that "among the leaders of Moscow's satellite intelligence services there was unanimous agreement that the KGB had been involved in the assassination of President Kennedy."<sup id="cite_ref-Pacepa0_449-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pacepa0-449">&#91;446&#93;</a></sup> Pacepa later released a book, <i>Programmed to Kill: Lee Harvey Oswald, the Soviet KGB, and the Kennedy Assassination</i>, in 2007. Similar views on the JFK assassination were expressed by Robert Holmes, former First Secretary at the British Embassy in Moscow, in his 2012 book <i>Spy Like No Other</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decoy_hearse_and_wound_alteration">Decoy hearse and wound alteration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Decoy hearse and wound alteration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Lifton" title="David Lifton">David Lifton</a> presented a scenario in which conspirators on <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_One" title="Air Force One">Air Force One</a> removed Kennedy's body from its original bronze casket and placed it in a shipping casket, while en route from Dallas to Washington. Once the presidential plane arrived at <a href="/wiki/Andrews_Air_Force_Base" title="Andrews Air Force Base">Andrews Air Force Base</a>, the shipping casket with the President's body in it was surreptitiously taken by helicopter from the side of the plane that was out of the television camera's view. Kennedy's body was then taken to an unknown location — most likely <a href="/wiki/Walter_Reed_Army_Medical_Center" title="Walter Reed Army Medical Center">Walter Reed Army Medical Center</a><sup id="cite_ref-450" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-450">&#91;447&#93;</a></sup> — to surgically alter the body to make it appear that he was shot only from the rear.<sup id="cite_ref-451" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-451">&#91;448&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKnight200795_452-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKnight200795-452">&#91;449&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wrone_453-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrone-453">&#91;450&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Turner,_Nigel_1988_454-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner,_Nigel_1988-454">&#91;451&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Part of Lifton's theory comes from a House Select Committee on Assassinations report of an interview of Lt. Richard Lipsey on January 18, 1978, by committee staff members Donald Purdy and Mark Flanagan. According to the report, Lt. Richard Lipsey said that he and General Wehle had met President Kennedy's body at Andrews Air Force Base. Lipsey "... placed [the casket] in a hearse to be transported to Bethesda Naval Hospital. Lipsey mentioned that he and Wehle then flew by helicopter to Bethesda and took [the body of] JFK into the back of Bethesda." Lipsey said that "a decoy hearse had been driven to the front [of Bethesda]".<sup id="cite_ref-455" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-455">&#91;452&#93;</a></sup> With Lipsey's mention of a "decoy hearse" at Bethesda, Lifton theorized that the casket removed by Lipsey from Air Force One — from the side of the plane exposed to television — was probably also a decoy and was likely empty.<sup id="cite_ref-456" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-456">&#91;453&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-457" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-457">&#91;454&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Laboratory technologist Paul O'Connor was one of the major witnesses supporting another part of David Lifton's theory that somewhere between Parkland and Bethesda the President's body was made to appear as if it had been shot only from the rear. O'Connor said that President Kennedy's body arrived at Bethesda inside a body bag in "a cheap, shipping-type of casket", which differed from the description of the ornamental bronze casket and sheet that the body had been wrapped in at Parkland Hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-Turner,_Nigel_1988_1_458-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner,_Nigel_1988_1-458">&#91;455&#93;</a></sup> O'Connor said that the brain had already been removed by the time it got to Bethesda,<sup id="cite_ref-Turner,_Nigel_1988_1_458-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner,_Nigel_1988_1-458">&#91;455&#93;</a></sup> and that there were "just little pieces" of brain matter left inside the skull.<sup id="cite_ref-459" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-459">&#91;456&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Researcher <a href="/wiki/David_Wrone" class="mw-redirect" title="David Wrone">David Wrone</a> dismissed the theory that Kennedy's body was surreptitiously removed from the presidential plane, stating that as is done with all cargo on airplanes for safety precautions, the coffin and lid were held by steel wrapping cables to prevent shifting during takeoff and landing and in case of air disturbances in flight.<sup id="cite_ref-Wrone_453-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrone-453">&#91;450&#93;</a></sup> According to Wrone, the side of the plane away from the television camera "was bathed in klieg lights, and thousands of persons watched along the fence that bent backward along that side, providing, in effect, a well-lit and very public stage for any would-be body snatchers".<sup id="cite_ref-Wrone_453-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrone-453">&#91;450&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_Reserve_conspiracy">Federal Reserve conspiracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Federal Reserve conspiracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Jim Marrs, in his book <i>Crossfire</i>, presented the theory that Kennedy was trying to rein in the power of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve" title="Federal Reserve">Federal Reserve</a>, and that forces opposed to such action might have played at least some part in the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989275_460-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrs1989275-460">&#91;457&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Silber_461-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silber-461">&#91;458&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Woodward_1996_462-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Woodward_1996-462">&#91;459&#93;</a></sup> According to Marrs, the issuance of <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_11110" title="Executive Order 11110">Executive Order 11110</a> was an effort by Kennedy to transfer power from the Federal Reserve to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Department of the Treasury">United States Department of the Treasury</a> by replacing <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Notes" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Reserve Notes">Federal Reserve Notes</a> with <a href="/wiki/Silver_certificate_(United_States)" title="Silver certificate (United States)">silver certificates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Silber_461-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silber-461">&#91;458&#93;</a></sup> Actor and author <a href="/wiki/Richard_Belzer" title="Richard Belzer">Richard Belzer</a> named the responsible parties in this theory as American "billionaires, power brokers, and bankers ... working in tandem with the CIA and other sympathetic agents of the government".<sup id="cite_ref-Belzer2_463-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belzer2-463">&#91;460&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2010 article in <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Research_(magazine)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Research (magazine) (page does not exist)">Research</a></i> magazine discussing various controversies surrounding the Federal Reserve stated that "the wildest accusation against the Fed is that it was involved in Kennedy's assassination."<sup id="cite_ref-Silber_461-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silber-461">&#91;458&#93;</a></sup> Critics of the theory note that Kennedy called for and signed legislation phasing out Silver Certificates in favor of Federal Reserve Notes, thereby enhancing the power of the Federal Reserve; and that Executive Order 11110 was a technicality that only delegated existing presidential powers to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Secretary of the Treasury">Secretary of the Treasury</a> for administrative convenience during a period of transition.<sup id="cite_ref-Silber_461-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silber-461">&#91;458&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Woodward_1996_462-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Woodward_1996-462">&#91;459&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israeli_government_conspiracy">Israeli government conspiracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Israeli government conspiracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Immediately following Kennedy's death, speculation that he was assassinated by a "<a href="/wiki/Antisemitic_conspiracy_theories" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic conspiracy theories">Zionist conspiracy</a>" was prevalent in much of the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Muslim world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bass_464-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bass-464">&#91;461&#93;</a></sup> Among these views were that <a href="/wiki/Zionist" class="mw-redirect" title="Zionist">Zionists</a> were motivated to kill Kennedy due to his opposition to an <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_Israel" title="Nuclear weapons and Israel">Israeli nuclear program</a>, that Lyndon B. Johnson received orders from Zionists to have Kennedy killed, and that the assassin was a Zionist agent.<sup id="cite_ref-Bass_464-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bass-464">&#91;461&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Michael_Collins_Piper" title="Michael Collins Piper">Michael Collins Piper</a> in <i>Final Judgment: The Missing Link in the JFK Assassination Controversy</i>, Israeli Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">David Ben-Gurion</a> orchestrated the assassination after learning that Kennedy planned to keep Israel from obtaining nuclear weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-Goldwag_465-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldwag-465">&#91;462&#93;</a></sup> Piper said that the assassination "was a joint enterprise conducted on the highest levels of the American CIA, in collaboration with organized crime — and most specifically, with direct and profound involvement by the Israeli intelligence service, the <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">Mossad</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-466" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-466">&#91;463&#93;</a></sup> The theory also alleges involvement of <a href="/wiki/Meyer_Lansky" title="Meyer Lansky">Meyer Lansky</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Goldwag_465-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldwag-465">&#91;462&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Mordechai_Vanunu" title="Mordechai Vanunu">Mordechai Vanunu</a> stated that the assassination was Israel's response to "pressure [Kennedy] exerted on ... Ben-Gurion, to shed light on <a href="/wiki/Negev_Nuclear_Research_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Negev Nuclear Research Center">Dimona's nuclear reactor in Israel</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-The_Sydney_Morning_Herald_467-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Sydney_Morning_Herald-467">&#91;464&#93;</a></sup> In a speech before the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> in 2009, Libyan leader <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a> also alleged that Kennedy was killed for wanting to investigate Dimona.<sup id="cite_ref-468" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-468">&#91;465&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_published_theories">Other published theories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Other published theories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hickey-ar-15_jfk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Hickey-ar-15_jfk.jpg/220px-Hickey-ar-15_jfk.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Hickey-ar-15_jfk.jpg/330px-Hickey-ar-15_jfk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Hickey-ar-15_jfk.jpg/440px-Hickey-ar-15_jfk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="309" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hickey-ar-15_jfk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Photo showing driver Agent George Hickey shortly after JFK was killed holding the <a href="/wiki/Colt_AR-15" title="Colt AR-15">AR-15</a> rifle that accidental shooting theorists say killed Kennedy.</div></div></div>
<ul><li><i>Reasonable Doubt</i> (1985) by Henry Hurt, who writes about his Warren Commission doubts. Hurt pins the plot on professional crook Robert Easterling, along with Texas oilmen and the supposed Ferrie/Shaw alliance. <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886058088">.mw-parser-output code.cs1-code{color:inherit;background:inherit;border:inherit;padding:inherit}.mw-parser-output .cs1-hidden-error{display:none;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-visible-error{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{display:none;color:#33aa33;margin-left:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration,.mw-parser-output .cs1-format{font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-left,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-left{padding-left:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-right{padding-right:0.2em}</style><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-03-004059-0" title="Special:BookSources/0-03-004059-0">0-03-004059-0</a>.</li>
<li><i>Behold a Pale Horse</i> (1991) by <a href="/wiki/Milton_William_Cooper" title="Milton William Cooper">William Cooper</a> alleges that Kennedy was shot by the presidential limousine's driver, Secret Service agent William Greer. In the Zapruder film, Greer can be seen turning to his right and looking backwards just before speeding away from Dealey Plaza. This theory has come under severe criticism from others in the research community.<sup id="cite_ref-469" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-469">&#91;466&#93;</a></sup> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-929385-22-5" title="Special:BookSources/0-929385-22-5">0-929385-22-5</a>.</li>
<li>Former Secret Service agent <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Bolden" title="Abraham Bolden">Abraham Bolden</a>'s <i>The Echo from Dealey Plaza</i> (2008) (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-307-38201-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-307-38201-6">978-0-307-38201-6</a>) and Kevin James Shay's <i>Death of the Rising Sun</i> (2017) (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-881-36556-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-881-36556-3">978-1-881-36556-3</a>) detail plots that occurred shortly before Kennedy's trip to Dallas in 1963, in Chicago and Florida. Within the Secret Service during those chaotic months, "rumors were flying" about Cuban dissidents and right-wing southerners who were stalking Kennedy for a chance to kill him, Bolden wrote. The security threat in Chicago in early November 1963 involved former Marine Thomas Arthur Vallee, who was arrested after police found an M-1 rifle, handgun, and 3,000 rounds of ammunition in his vehicle. A high-powered rifle was confiscated from another suspected conspirator in Chicago shortly before Kennedy's trip there was canceled, Bolden said. Authorities also cited similar threats in Tampa, Fla., and Miami about a week later.</li>
<li>Mark North's <i>Act of Treason: The Role of J. Edgar Hoover in the Assassination of President Kennedy,</i> (1991) implicates the FBI Director. North documents that Hoover was aware of threats against Kennedy by organized crime before 1963, and suggests that he failed to take proper action to prevent the assassination. North also charges Hoover with failure to work adequately to uncover the truth behind Kennedy's murder, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-88184-877-8" title="Special:BookSources/0-88184-877-8">0-88184-877-8</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Mortal_Error:_The_Shot_That_Killed_JFK" class="mw-redirect" title="Mortal Error: The Shot That Killed JFK">Mortal Error: The Shot That Killed JFK</a></i> (1992) by Bonar Menninger (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-312-08074-3" title="Special:BookSources/0-312-08074-3">0-312-08074-3</a>) alleges that while Oswald did attempt to assassinate JFK and did succeed in wounding him, the shot that struck him in the head was accidentally fired by Secret Service agent George Hickey, who was riding in the Secret Service follow-up car directly behind the presidential limousine. The theory alleges that after the first two shots were fired the motorcade sped up while Hickey was attempting to respond to Oswald's shots and he lost his balance and accidentally pulled the trigger of his <a href="/wiki/AR-15" class="mw-redirect" title="AR-15">AR-15</a> and shot JFK. Hickey's testimony says otherwise: "<i>At the end of the last report</i> (shot) I reached to the bottom of the car and picked up the AR 15 rifle, cocked and loaded it, <i>and turned to the rear.</i>" (italics added).<sup id="cite_ref-470" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-470">&#91;467&#93;</a></sup> George Hickey sued Menninger in April 1995 for what he had written in <i>Mortal Error</i>. The case was dismissed as its <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_limitations" title="Statute of limitations">statute of limitations</a> had run out. The theory received public attention in 2013 when it was supported by <a href="/wiki/Colin_McLaren" title="Colin McLaren">Colin McLaren</a>'s book and documentary titled <i><a href="/wiki/Colin_McLaren#JFK:_The_Smoking_Gun" title="Colin McLaren">JFK: The Smoking Gun</a></i> (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7336-3044-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7336-3044-6">978-0-7336-3044-6</a>).</li>
<li><i>Who Shot JFK?&#160;: A Guide to the Major Conspiracy Theories</i> (1993) by Bob Callahan and Mark Zingarelli explores some of the more obscure theories regarding JFK's murder, such as "The Coca-Cola Theory". According to this theory, suggested by the editor of an organic gardening magazine, Oswald killed JFK due to mental impairment stemming from an addiction to refined sugar, as evidenced by his need for his favorite beverage immediately after the assassination. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-671-79494-9" title="Special:BookSources/0-671-79494-9">0-671-79494-9</a>.</li>
<li><i>Passport to Assassination</i> (1993) by Oleg M. Nechiporenko, the Soviet consular official (and highly placed KGB officer) who met with Oswald in Mexico City in 1963. He was afforded the unique opportunity to interview Oswald about his goals including his genuine desire for a Cuban visa. His conclusions were: (1) that Oswald killed Kennedy due to extreme feelings of inadequacy versus his wife's professed admiration for JFK, and (2) that the KGB never sought intelligence information from Oswald during his time in the USSR as they did not trust his motivations. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-55972-210-X" title="Special:BookSources/1-55972-210-X">1-55972-210-X</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norman_Mailer" title="Norman Mailer">Norman Mailer</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Oswald%27s_Tale:_An_American_Mystery" class="mw-redirect" title="Oswald&#39;s Tale: An American Mystery">Oswald's Tale: An American Mystery</a></i> (1995) concludes that Oswald was guilty, but holds that the evidence may point to a second gunman on the grassy knoll, who, purely by coincidence, was attempting to kill JFK at the same time as Oswald. "If there was indeed another shot, it was not necessarily fired by a conspirator of Oswald's. Such a gun could have belonged to another lone killer or to a conspirator working for some other group altogether."<sup id="cite_ref-471" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-471">&#91;468&#93;</a></sup> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-679-42535-7" title="Special:BookSources/0-679-42535-7">0-679-42535-7</a>.</li>
<li><i>The Kennedy Mutiny</i> (2002) by Will Fritz (not the same as police captain J. Will Fritz), claims that the assassination plot was orchestrated by General <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Walker" title="Edwin Walker">Edwin Walker</a>, and that he framed Oswald for the crime. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-9721635-0-6" title="Special:BookSources/0-9721635-0-6">0-9721635-0-6</a>.</li>
<li><i>JFK: The Second Plot</i> (2002) by Matthew Smith explores the strange case of Roscoe White. In 1990, Roscoe's son Ricky made public a claim that his father, who had been a Dallas police officer in 1963, was involved in killing the president. Roscoe's widow Geneva also claimed that before her husband's death in 1971 he left a diary in which he claims he was one of the marksmen who shot the President, and that he also killed <a href="/wiki/J._D._Tippit" title="J. D. Tippit">Officer J. D. Tippit</a>. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-84018-501-5" title="Special:BookSources/1-84018-501-5">1-84018-501-5</a>.</li>
<li>David Wrone's <i>The Zapruder Film</i> (2003) concludes that the shot that killed JFK came from in front of the limousine, and that JFK's throat and back wounds were caused by an in-and-through shot originating from the grassy knoll. Three shots were fired from three different angles, none of them from Lee Harvey Oswald's window at the Texas School Book Depository. Wrone is a professor of history (emeritus) at the University of Wisconsin–Stevens Point. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-7006-1291-2" title="Special:BookSources/0-7006-1291-2">0-7006-1291-2</a>.</li>
<li><i>The <a href="/wiki/Gemstone_File" title="Gemstone File">Gemstone File</a>: A Memoir</i> (2006), by Stephanie Caruana, posits that Oswald was part of a 28-man assassination team that included three U.S. Mafia hitmen (<a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Fratianno" title="Jimmy Fratianno">Jimmy Fratianno</a>, John Roselli, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eugene_Brading&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eugene Brading (page does not exist)">Eugene Brading</a>). Oswald's role was to shoot John Connally. Bruce Roberts, author of the Gemstone File papers, claimed that the JFK assassination scenario was modeled after a supposed attempted assassination of President F.D. Roosevelt. Roosevelt was riding in an open car with Mayor <a href="/wiki/Anton_Cermak" title="Anton Cermak">Anton Cermak</a> of Chicago. Cermak was shot and killed by <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Zangara" title="Giuseppe Zangara">Giuseppe Zangara</a>. In Dallas, JFK was the real target, and Connally was a secondary target. The JFK assassination is only a small part of the Gemstone File's account. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-4120-6137-7" title="Special:BookSources/1-4120-6137-7">1-4120-6137-7</a>.</li>
<li>Joseph P. Farrell's <i>LBJ and the Conspiracy to Kill Kennedy</i> (2011) attempts to show multiple interests had reasons to remove President Kennedy: The military, CIA, NASA, anti-Castro factions, Hoover's FBI and others. He concludes that the person that allowed all of these groups to form a "coalescence of interests" was Vice President Lyndon Johnson. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-935487-18-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-935487-18-0">978-1-935487-18-0</a></li>
<li>In "Allegations of PFC Eugene Dinkin",<sup id="cite_ref-472" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-472">&#91;469&#93;</a></sup> the Mary Farrell Foundation summarizes and archives documents related to Private First Class Eugene B. Dinkin, a cryptographic code operator stationed in <a href="/wiki/Metz,_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Metz, France">Metz, France</a>, who went <a href="/wiki/AWOL" class="mw-redirect" title="AWOL">AWOL</a> in early November 1963, entered Switzerland using a false ID, and visited the United Nations' press office and declared that officials in the U.S. government were planning to assassinate President Kennedy, adding that "something" might happen to the Commander in Chief in Texas. Dinkin was arrested nine days before Kennedy was killed, placed in psychiatric care (deemed a mad man?), and released shortly thereafter. His allegations eventually made their way to the Warren Commission, but, according to the Ferrell Foundation account, the Commission "took no interest in the matter, and indeed omitted any mention of Dinkin from its purportedly encyclopedic 26 volumes of evidence."<sup id="cite_ref-473" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-473">&#91;470&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Described by the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> as "one of the strangest theories",<sup id="cite_ref-The_Victoria_Advocate;_November_23,_1975_474-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Victoria_Advocate;_November_23,_1975-474">&#91;471&#93;</a></sup> Hugh McDonald's <i>Appointment in Dallas</i> stated that the Soviet government <a href="/wiki/Contract_killing" title="Contract killing">contracted</a> with a rogue CIA agent named "Saul" to have Kennedy killed.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Miami_News;_January_20,_1976_475-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Miami_News;_January_20,_1976-475">&#91;472&#93;</a></sup> McDonald said he worked for the CIA "on assignment for $100 a day" and met "Saul" at <a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Center_for_Intelligence" title="George Bush Center for Intelligence">the Agency's headquarters</a> after the Bay of Pigs Invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Philadelphia_Bulletin;_December_8,_1975_476-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Philadelphia_Bulletin;_December_8,_1975-476">&#91;473&#93;</a></sup> According to McDonald, his CIA mentor told him that "Saul" was the world's best assassin.<sup id="cite_ref-Evening_Independent;_November_27,_1975_477-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evening_Independent;_November_27,_1975-477">&#91;474&#93;</a></sup> McDonald stated that after the assassination, he recognized the man's photo in the Warren Commission report and eventually tracked him to a London hotel in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Philadelphia_Bulletin;_December_8,_1975_476-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Philadelphia_Bulletin;_December_8,_1975-476">&#91;473&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Evening_Independent;_November_27,_1975_477-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evening_Independent;_November_27,_1975-477">&#91;474&#93;</a></sup> McDonald stated that "Saul" assumed he, too, was a CIA agent and confided to him that he shot Kennedy from a building on the other side of the street from the Texas School Book Depository.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Victoria_Advocate;_November_23,_1975_474-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Victoria_Advocate;_November_23,_1975-474">&#91;471&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>[Torbitt, William]. (1970) <i>Nomenclature On An Assassination Cabal</i>.  The pseudonymous author claimed to be a lawyer with investigative skills working in the South.  See <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/nsia-NomenclatureoftheAssassinationCabal-TorbittDocument/page/n0">The Internet Archive website</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Two years after the publication of the Warren Report, Commission member Senator Richard Russell expressed doubt with parts of the Report. In a November 20, 1966 interview with <i>The Atlanta Constitution</i>, Russell said he harbored a "lingering dissatisfaction" with the Commission's work and that he disagreed with the single bullet theory. On Jan. 19, 1970, Russell again proclaimed his doubts in a television interview, saying that he "never believed that Lee Harvey Oswald assassinated President Kennedy without at least some encouragement from others." Russell added: "I think someone else worked with him." <a href="#CITEREFHSCA_Report">HSCA Report</a>, p.&#160;14, <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.aarclibrary.org/publib/jfk/hsca/reportvols/vol11/pdf/HSCA_Vol11_WC_1_Operations.pdf">[1]</a>, Vol. 11</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-150"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-150">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In Bill Newman's voluntary statement to the Sheriff's Department, signed and notarized on November 22, 1963, he wrote that the gunshot "had come from the garden directly behind me, that was on an elevation from where I was as I was right on the curb. I do not recall looking toward the Texas School Book Depository. I looked back in the vacinity &#32;&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>&#93; of the garden."&#91;<a href="#CITEREFWarren_Commission_Hearings1964">Warren Commission Hearings 1964</a>, Vol. XIX, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.maryferrell.org/mffweb/archive/viewer/showDoc.do?docId=1136&amp;relPageId=508">p. 490</a>&#93;</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-276"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-276">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the Warren Commission, after Earlene Roberts saw Oswald standing near the bus stop outside his rooming house, "[he] was next seen about nine-tenths of a mile (1.4 km) away at the southeast corner of 10th Street and Patton Avenue, moments before the Tippit shooting."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964165_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReport_of_the_President&#39;s_Commission_on_the_Assassination_of_President_John_F._Kennedy,_Chapter_41964165-275">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-HCSA-IC-339"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-HCSA-IC_339-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-HCSA-IC_339-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-HCSA-IC_339-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-HCSA-IC_339-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-HCSA-IC_339-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-HCSA-IC_339-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.archives.gov/research/jfk/select-committee-report/part-1c.html">"I.C. The committee believes, on the basis of the evidence available to it, that President John F. Kennedy was probably assassinated as a result of a conspiracy.
